O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I completed this with a treatise, which is the part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is practiced extensively in our region and is strange to all, the knowledge has been lost and cut off, and there is no longer any record of its power other than small descriptions in old books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, error and vanity have arisen, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by organizing it according to the order of exposition and explanation, and by providing an overview; I will bring together the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools used in the work, along with adjustments to their declaration and preparation, as is required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins, and the number of their branches, and how they move and rest, and from where they emanate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that knowledge without practice is useless, and practice without knowledge is dangerous; especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks falling into error and misleading others; as I have often seen happen with many who undertake this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a terrible sight, which affected the scrofula of the neck of a woman, and it affected the arteries of her neck; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in the woman's hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another strange sight where a stone was removed from an old man's bladder; the stone was large. It took with it a piece of the bladder wall and the man suffered for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if it was not cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another wonder which took in hand the treatment of our land's duke who had a broken leg, and with the fracture he had an open wound; and all the learned, out of ignorance, held fast to the fracture over the wound as if by strong bonds, leaving no space for the wound to heal, and left it thus until the end; and ordered that he should not loosen it; and so delayed that the leg became completely swollen and painful, and eventually perished.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I quickly went to loosen the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, it was as if in peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another wonder that the abscess, which had been healed, then burst again due to the malignancy of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from melancholic humor, it is not appropriate to apply iron if it is not in a place where everything that is corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, work involving danger in various ways; and I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, guard against any vain imagination that the foolish might speak ill of you. Take up your weapons with courage and undertake your sick with gentleness and firmness, using the best means so that by God's grace you may find salvation and be saved; banish diseases filled with despair through health; lay down your arms if they cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take any illness too seriously, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and the use of bitter medicine, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of poultices and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered and includes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it provides instructions for using the right tools from head to foot, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, in remembering the work, it is necessary that I describe the qualities of each aid and its harmful effects on each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harmful effects are the most extensive knowledge and subtle science, and these secrets are revealed; and many wise men spoke of them and agreed upon this; and I will content myself with a few words, as I fear lengthening this discussion.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every condition where it has matter, whether it be hot or dry conditions: that is to say, a hot condition with material, and a dry condition without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry conditions, matter is present, and they devised different opinions, some saying that cautery is great help, and others saying the opposite: that cautery is of no use for diseases arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for hot diseases, neither by heat nor dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help for hot and dry diseases that come upon the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture to the complexion affected by fire, you feel the body is hot.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt it unless they have tried it themselves, and know through long experience the chapter of cautery, and the variety of human complexes, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and the passage of time; for other complexes we only have fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and assembled around the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, son, that cautery brings together fire, which is a secret of healing, and moreover, it is much gentler than medicinal burning cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	Because fire is simple, and it does not come from outside the burned member, and it does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicinal burn treatments travel from one member to another, and they cause the afflicted member grief and prevent healing; and sometimes the fire does not harm the patient because of its high quality and the goodness of its substance, as long as it is not excessive.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And because I have found it through experience and the long service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in accordance with the truth of the matter, I will excuse myself for the length of the speech, for I do not like to deprive you of the secret hidden within fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when cauterization should be performed and the best tools to use.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the pain-relieving effect of cauterization removes the harm; and indeed, cauterization is often necessary in cases of severe and urgent pain that cannot wait for a more serious illness to affect the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who follow folly; for the illness that is healed by cautery has no return; and it must be so. But it is not like how they care for it, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and moves more quickly than other medicines due to the worth of its action and mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another thing that must be known is that the illness comes according to the state of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and excesses accumulate within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cauterization is applied in moderation where there is little excess and moisture, as in the cauterization for pain and similar conditions, and this kind of pain does not return; but that happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and that's true; but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, for when we administer treatments in any illness, and they are useless, then let us use cautery, and it will be beneficial.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not at all according to the understanding of ignorant people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are better than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for the quality of the gold and for the nobility of its substance; and they said that the heat of cautery does not burn, but this is not true, as I have experienced it myself, and I have found that it does indeed burn in everyone; and gold cautery is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you are not certain if it is hot through and through because of its golden color, and as soon as it cools down; and if it is overheated, it becomes damaged; thus there is ample hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery because we have equipped ourselves with the necessary tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	You have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the way may be easier to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Cyst cauterization is applied to the brain using moisture and cold, and it is effective for conditions caused by a disease called "soda" and due to many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for frequent dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially for diseases arising from cold, such as paralysis, soda (a term possibly referring to a type of stroke), apoplexy, and similar conditions.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient is purged with a solvent medicine, cleansing the head, either three times or four, according to the virtue, age, and custom of the patient's illness; and then the head is allowed to dry again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it rest crossed in your hands, placing his hands on both sides of his body; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two fingers; and let where your thumb and forefinger meet, if it bleeds, then heat up the cautery called 'olive', which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mark the location with an ink sign, and repeatedly descend and stretch your hand while gently trembling; then lift your hand carefully, and check if you see the bone move slightly; if not, repeat the cauterization until you see the bone as I have told you. Afterwards, take some string, put dry and soft cotton inside, place it on the wound, and leave it for three days; then cover it with butter-moistened cotton, and keep it until the scalding is gone; finally, treat the wound with a preparation called 'tetrafarmacy' while it remains clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older the wound, the more it purifies itself; and for this reason, it requires more help.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not leave the fire cautery to burn off part of the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one should leave the cautery for a long time, and pull so hard to reduce the bone as if women were opening their wombs to let humors flow out; and one should keep the wound open for a long time; after which, it must be cleaned and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except for those who have no choice but to suffer; and I think I should leave them; because the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, just as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this I use it accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills called "cough drops", as well as applications of poultices; and if one performs the cautery that we have mentioned above, it will be ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's joint is of strong nature and not too frozen; then cauterize it from below, using the cautery as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the shoulder joint, as we said before, and cauterizing the one called "vessel," which is where the suction cups are placed, hold your hand aloft so that you do not see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak of it then; it is necessary that the cautery of the horns be more precise than that of the middle part of the shoulder, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or perhaps the brain), and the condition is purged with medicines according to the methods described in the division of diseases, and all these treatments are ineffective, then one must resort to cautery, according to two methods: that is, using hot medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with hot medicine is when you heat a piece of alder, remove the bark and dip it in the wound as deep as the tissue, and then make an incision where the pain is located in such a way that you can push the alder under the skin; and when it is pushed under, hold it there tightly for twelve hours. Then release it and treat the wound with hot compresses for two to three days, after which apply a plug soaked in butter until the infection subsides.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the healing treatment, as long as it is healthy; and if you see that something similar to what I have written about burning medications or the dosage for treating them has been done.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery instrument with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a clot with a small amount of curd, and in the middle there is a slight appearance; place it on the painful area, hold your hand, and turn it slightly so that half of the thickness of the heart is burned; then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is dangerous, and an abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in awe of the string, and putting it on the joint for three days; then he covers it with moistened butter, and then dresses the joint with medicine until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have previously described in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned provides no help, then you must reheat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white; then seal over the painful joint with a line half a finger's length long, and remove your hand once, so as not to cover the artery and not let blood come out; be careful of the jaw that moves when chewing, and let the nerve pay no mind except to move and avoid spasms from affecting the patient; be wary of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, especially for someone who lacks knowledge or experience, and leave the work in the middle. But I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and show you where in this book it is mentioned.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice against the disease, and the patient suffers, burn the affected area again as we have said, and treat the wound until it is clean; and if you observe, apply the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of arteries, with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than the other.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	regarding the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and various soothing medicines and other treatments as mentioned in our divisions have been applied, but the pain persists, then use this cautery called "point," which has the following form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After puncturing the entire painful ear, or both ears if they hold pain in either, and pulling slightly away from the root of the ear after marking the place with a sign, take ten points around each ear; then treat the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that requires cautery is limited to those that involve fluid movement, as we have discussed in the sections on disease; and do not perform cautery on areas that exhibit dryness, rust, or nerve pain.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this kind of pain that mutates from fluid of water and purging from the head and gargarism, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little farther down the temple, and the third on the adjustment of the two lips; and place the cautery in the part that opens healthily, and make the cautery on the top of the ear above a little below the brow, and another in the temple just as far; and leave the cautery until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the cutting tool that we have previously mentioned, but it is a little more subtle, and it is necessary for the knife to be slightly thicker; after that, treat it as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: two on the two horns of the head, one on the forehead, and one on the liver, which is called "vassel," as we have previously mentioned, and do not cauterize anything on the mouth of the stomach; treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	De litargie" translates directly to "on lith
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large and pure mental rest; then gently turn the head of the sick person, and place on his forehead an application of mustard plaster, as described in the preparation of plasters; and this is the manner of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy thus, good; and if it is not, make three cauterizations on the inside of the thigh down to the bone, and leave two large spaces between each cauterization, and treat it as the others, and if you see it becoming inflamed, and the patient is suffering, make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and treat until it is healthy; and this cauterization called 'olivare' as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold at the top
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with earth and water as we have said before; then wash the patient's head, make a cauterization between the chief and each horn, and three on the spine of the collarbone; and if you need it, and the flesh is moist and the patient suffers and the illness is severe, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave it until the most tender heart is burned, and then ease your hand. After that, treat until it is healthy, and this cauterization called 'olivare' as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery unless they are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other treatments that we have discussed in the section on great pain and suffering from medicinal failure.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an evil spirit that cannot endure this, then gargle and chew, purifying the brain often with good meats; after the ruler places his head in the middle, perform cautery as we have said before, and cauterize the veins and each horn. And if the patient is weak and suffering, perform cautery as I have said to one with paralysis and softening of the limbs, on the spine and neck, and cauterize with olive oil according to the manner that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is ill, perform a delicate cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are excessive or corrupted moisture and thick fluxes, then perform cauterization with partial cautery as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the excessive moisture declines into melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain may be purified, as it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After preparing the patient's head, make an incision around it neatly, just as you would draw a circle, and place it back on the head; let the patient lie with their eyes crossed and firmly held from all sides; then apply the dressing, and use a small amount of old sheep butter; warm the mixture at a moderate fire, so that the patient can bear it; afterward empty the circle inside the head, and leave it to cool; and repeat this treatment for the patient once each week with another suitable remedy until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you must cauterize it, make several small incisions throughout the cauterization.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the skin increasingly; then place cotton soaked in butter and gelatine upon it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes first show signs of displacement as described in the previous section, then treatment begins and the patient is given something to drink, a purifying remedy for the head, and care is taken of all moisture, and sudorifacient or bath is administered several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After instructing the patient to look straight ahead, he should be made to gaze up at the ceiling, and then two cauterizations are performed on both temples if the eye movement is in both directions together, or separately if it moves only in one; all veins and arteries beneath the heart should be carefully cauterized, and the cautery should be long according to the width of the temple, and care must be taken to prevent bloodletting, and if too much blood issues, it should be stopped as you see fit.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you, in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, how to do it carefully; and never should one cauterize or burn the bones from behind.
dou cors des larmes	The pain of the heart.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are long-standing and habitual, and are in the veins, where the arteries are visible, then one should apply the fire cautery that I spoke of at the beginning of this chapter: one cauterizes over the eye, and two cauterizes on both temples, and two cauterizes behind the bones; and if more is needed, one cauterizes sharply across the eyebrow with all the small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Let the body weep through the eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the previous section, and it does not improve, then give the patient three drops of a mixture of herbs; after warming his head, perform cauterization in the middle of the cautery with olive oil; make two cauterizations on each shoulder with the cautery called 'clavilis', slightly below the hairline; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the skin is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery which is called "olive-style".
de coi ci est li forme:	Due to which the form is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you perform the cauterization on both sides of the wound as long as the scars are; and do not let go of the instrument until one-third of the skin is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that is not yet oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time does it happen that the hair of the wound is converted to a different color, and it pricks, and one performs cauterization according to two manners: namely, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in a clean bed; next, draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as large as the wound is deep, and make it at the beginning of the sign among the hairs; then apply moist cotton in egg white and musk from persil over the wound, and then heat the cauterizing iron with this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the affected area little by little, burn the surrounding skin; and the signs of healing are that you see the paper-like skin retreating, and the hairs standing up at the tip of the oil; then gently release your hand and leave it for three days, after which apply moistened cotton in butter until the burning is gone; subsequently, continue treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs grow back, and the paper-like skin becomes soft, then resume cauterizing in the same place as before; and if the hairs are burned, cauterize again while the skin is raised to its natural state, and it is even, and the hairs do not poke into the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal fire cauterization is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment shape of the leaf of mirta (myrrh). Take French soap and bright charcoal, each in equal parts, and grind them together thoroughly; apply it gently so as not to chill, then spread it over the form made like the leaf of myrrh, and place paper on top. If the illness persists in one oil only, one must operate in one way, and similarly for both. Put cotton soaked in warm oil underneath, and the afflicted part should be in your healthy hand; apply your finger showing the medicine, press gently and slowly every time the patient feels the sting of the medicine, because it stings as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	As you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, raise the limb from below, and reward if you see the papery skin raised as it was before by constraint of fire or incision; and if it is thus, so it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the limb, as long as your work is even and your fingers precise; then place moistened cotton on it until the burning of the herbs is extinguished, after which cure the limb with the dressing called 'dyafenis' and others, as long as it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have to take care of yourself, guard your work carefully so that it does not deviate from the cure at all.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hairs poke in the oil, repeat the treatment on that place which has become soft from the paper, just as you did before; then cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the poultice with great care.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the needs of men vary in size and extent, and according to your circumstances; and do not turn away from the right path those who have study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed in the sections on illnesses, and your treatments are not helping, then you must perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in a healthy position, and hold their arm's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or wiggle, keeping their head still. Afterwards, apply moist cotton or persil juice over the oil. Next, heat up the cautery tool until it is hot enough. Position it on the head, making sure it covers the entire area like a feather, or like a tent, but at all times, ensure that the edge of the cautery is curved for your convenience.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and dry it; if it closes again, repeat the process and apply hot cautery; hold your hand over the cautery at the affected area above the oil, so that your hand does not cause harm; place the cautery on the fat of the oil and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cautery close to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cauterization once more, or as many times as necessary, and leave it for three days; then apply moist cotton in butter, and continue the treatment of the drying dressing until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is still not healed, apply a corrosive medicine to the exposed bone; and the remedy should be according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for a fistula that no one among the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula and locate its origin; then, place a fine, sharp tool into the gap, thereby forming:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it in the quantity of a drop of blood; and hold your hand firm, so that the patient does not move at all, until the splint is completely formed; and it is necessary to put a piece of moist cotton on the wound to prevent infection or harm: the splint will loosen the fistula from its place and heal it wonderfully.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this does not happen, it is necessary to administer warmth or cold, and return the ulcer to the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks appear in the lips, called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	As you treat these wounds of which we spoke in detail, and the cure does not benefit, then heat a small surgical knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	and insert it into the wounds until it reaches the bottom; then treat the skin with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root or tonsil, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction, swelling, and becomes a fistula; then you treat it as we spoke about in detail, but it does not help: in this case, you need to perform cautery according to the size of the fistula. Remove or open the fistula's hole, and keep your hand there until the heat from the fire reaches the bottom, without touching anything else; do this once or twice after treating it as we described for wounds, until it heals; and if treated in this way, it will heal well. If not, you need to expose the affected area and remove any rotten bone, as is explained in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	without any joint movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it does not help, then put the afflicted part of the mouth in a healthy place; afterwards, heat the cautery with which the shape will come as if you placed a candle on the tooth; and insert the hot cautery deeply, holding your hand until the patient feels the warmth reaching the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; after that, have the patient fill his mouth with salty water and leave it for an hour or so.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the teeth that were moving will be firmly set, the gums that were softened will be restrained, and the moisture corrupted will dry up.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of teeth comes from coldness or frost or chill, and medical remedies are ineffective, then it is necessary to apply cauterization in two ways: with butter cautery or fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	For butter cautery, take some butter and press it into a spoon made of iron or silver; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a stick, soak it in melted butter, and apply it to the aching tooth with patience until it cools; do this repeatedly until its effect reaches the root of the tooth. If you find that the moisture from the wool and cotton has evaporated, and you apply the butter again while holding the hot iron over the aching tooth, then the heat will reach the nerve of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you can insert a piece of iron or steel, making it large enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; then, after heating the cautery, its shape will form as follows, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be lessened on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, and then quickly takes it out; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform cautery on the upper lip where you wish, according to your ability; and this is the shape of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of cold moisture, and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then apply heat to the cautery, so that after this, there are openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery in the other part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or as it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its quantity, leaving it thus for three days; and then apply moist cotton with butter until the burn is healed; after that, treat the wound with oil and bandages until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the wound:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it arises from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be relieved by solvent medicines; afterward, he should have cauterization at the root of the throat, and beware not to go near the throat, and only apply warmth gently.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, he performs another cauterization at the joint of the collarbone with the top of the spine, and these cauterizations called "clavicle" which we have described above; treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any sickness of the head are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or rigour, and if it is an old illness, then make two cauterizations on strong parts of his body; and another cauterization between the two members; and this cauterization which is called 'clavile' should be according to the shape mentioned above.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because cautery is lighter, because you do it three times as often.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach while it is being drained of its humors, the catarrh increases in him and the usual remedies are ineffective, then the patient should be careful on his back, extending his legs and hands.

Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you are cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach at one point according to the amount you see fit; then cauterize the entire cautery called 'point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously mentioned, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain from gallstones, moisture, and excessive flatulence due to excesses, and it is out of its natural state, the patient is treated as we have previously mentioned, which does not benefit them. It is necessary for the patient to rest on their head, and signs of three cauterizations should be made according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, removing the bad humors from where they originate; there should be enough space between each cauterization, about the thickness of a finger. The cauterization should be long in duration but do not press too hard with your hand over the entire cautery; burn only the middle part of the liver gently, and the patient should be on their feet with their legs extended and bras relaxed. This is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these wounds with a steel instrument, if you are skillful and wise in the art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would cause great damage throughout the body; and do not let it come to boiling, for the blood vessels are very delicate in this place, and only the skilled will see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is inside or around the liver: if it is inside, the patient feels a moderate level of pain; but if it is around the liver, they feel excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires attention, the patient must rest his head; then he should apply a signet to the joint where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a rose, in the following manner:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the veins are burned, and the pus comes out completely; after the cure, according to the treatment of the wounds, as long as it is healed; and it is not appropriate for this cautery to be used by anyone other than someone who has studied medicine extensively and whose hands have never failed in treating these illnesses.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can safely move it, but I still think it's better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of tears" does not appear to be a standard medical term in medieval
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should perform cautery on tears with the root of an herb called "aristologe", and in this way: take a long root of aristologe, the largest you can find, dry it, and make it as thick and as long as your hand; moisten it in oil, hold it over the fire, and cauterize between the eyebrows and the bridge of the nose, and small cautery a little lower on the face below the beard; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind; and another cautery across the middle, and another on the stomach, and between the shoulders, and along both sides of the lower ribs, deflating the cautery between the shoulders. Do not press your hand down, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. de la mice	of the mouse

de ydropisie	Dyshydrasia" is the modern term for

After that, make two cauterizations on each leg, at the tip of a sharp knife; and let the cauterization be long, one on the inside of the knee joint and the other on the outside, along the leg; and leave the cauterizations to heal for a long time without cleaning, so that the wound heals; then cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the joint
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the problem in the stomach comes from cold and moisture, weakening the retention and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and intestines, and it cannot be cured by any means; then you see the patient suffering greatly and possessing great strength, so perform a strong cautery on the stomach as he has spoken of before, according to the cautery for the stomach, with subtle fires around, and three fires on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundance of moisture and the patient suffering, perform a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each joint, and small cauterizations on the stomach to lessen the great pain, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are of old standing and consist of corrupt, cold, moist humors, they are treated as we have said in the previous divisions, but they do not benefit from cauterization.  Make three incisions along the spine of the back, starting from the bottom and working upwards in a triangular pattern; one cauterization below the anus two fingers deep; if you believe the stomach is chilled, the meat does not cook, and there is bloating visible on the face, then apply a hot cauterization to the stomach as mentioned above, and another to the liver, and yet another across the entire area with a heated iron; leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the joint as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness called "thelul", if the cautery appears too sharp, then cover it entirely with a hot compress; leave it until the heat reaches the vein, causing no harm. Do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelul" (flesh), cauterize each part as we have said before; afterward, apply beneficial remedies as long as they are healed, and if you cauterize a large area with a hot tool, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	From the poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate in its place, such a disease arises that can only be healed by cautery.
