Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a vein becomes fistulated, swollen, and discharged with putrid pus and corrupt moisture, you must try all subtle remedies, and be sure to know the effect of each remedy in detail.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery to a sharp point, insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the tentacle has entered, and repeat the cautery as many times as necessary—once, twice, or three times—depending on the quantity of corrupt and putrid material; and be careful not to burn the sensitive nerves or large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	He punctures the bladder and intestines, if you guard these joints, and do not make fires except in the flesh, and think that it is not harmful; afterward cure the joint as long as it is healthy, and if the joints are stable and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the joint is entirely healthy; and if the matter is not removed, know that the joint is weak, and the bone is corrupted at the bottom, just as we will say about one of these in its place.
de la maladie des reins	regarding the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of kidney stones and severe windiness comes and does not allow a woman to bear it, then you must perform cautery on the kidneys from both sides with a cauterizing iron that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and it will bring greater relief.
de la vessie	from the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from fluid and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then it should be cauterized in the upper part on top of the bladder where they begin to feel hair, both on the right and left sides, and each cautery should be as long as a finger; and also cauterize it at the back if necessary; and make the cauteries shaped as mentioned above.
de la marris	of the mare (female horse)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wound is cold and moist, it does not allow healing, and the flowers (scabs) form poorly and take a long time to fall off; when they do come off, great pain is felt. Then it is necessary to perform three cauterizations around the wound, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and these cauterizations should be done with a nail, as we have said.
de la hainche	The term "de la hainche" is not present in the
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the chest of the hinch (a term for a condition affecting the joints), this causes it to be immobile, and the signs are that the affected leg appears longer than the other when measured together; there is a visible swelling in the affected joint, and it is necessary to cauterize the patient above the chest of the hinch with a circular cauterization, marking around the joint as it moves, so that the joint remains within the circle; and the cauterization should be similar to that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present for you, then make three cauterizations from the large olive, and let the cauterization be as perfect as all the others; and treat until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the back, due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured as we have said in the previous section, but the treatment is ineffective, and the illness is chronic, then you must purge the patient of the bad humors with foul or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterward, he performs cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, altogether burning medications, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is performed in many ways, of which some are: You cauterize along the ribcage, making three triangular cauterizations according to this form, ensuring sufficient depth and width, with a space between each cauterization equal to the thickness of two fingers, and they are olive-shaped. Never perform cautery in the middle of the chest, for there should be three according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the cautery around the circle that we have spoken of in the dislocation of the shoulder; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all the shoulder, and all the parts of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain is localized in the shoulder and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain reaches the thigh and the leg, make two cauterizations at the point where the patient feels the pain, and one on top of the ankle, slightly to the left; these cauterizations should be with a cutting instrument, and they should burn the thick parts of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain spreads towards the knee or near it, cauterize there, at the point where he feels the pain, three times or four times with the cautery called "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain comes from the knee towards the thigh, he should perform a cautery with a cutting or circular instrument, and be very careful in all his cauterizations so that he does not leave them untreated for too long, lest he burn the nerves and major arteries, and do further harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	I myself have seen many who have performed a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left them until the leg was completely swollen, and the ankle as well, it became pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal solution, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform cautery on both, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones say about cautery for the hinch, which is the manner, take a needle of iron, also as thick as a new date or slightly thinner, and make it intertwined from one side to the other with spaces the size of a thumb's nail; interweave them across both parts, making them as straight as possible, and use a well-made iron tool; this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it turns completely red and begins to exude blisters, then place it on the wound of the diseased hinch, and turn towards its healthy side; perform cauterization once again after the first cautery, leaving it for three days; then apply a paste of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time until it heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to the danger of its power, and we should see few who employ it; nonetheless, these are good cauteries, which one can endure, and where they are needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The hot medical cautery is made by attaching a tool with a descending edge to a handle, either of iron or steel, mounted on a long pole. It should have a width of about the thickness of a finger and be open both below and above, joining together in this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the hot plate of the cautery on the patient's healthy side, and quickly covering your hand with a cloth over the plate, pour between the two circles of the hot awl, which has been heated over the fire, and leave it for an hour, allowing the patient to feel the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it has true cauterization just like fire; and when the cauterization is passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hair gently, leaving it for three days, and apply butter until the blackness from the burn disappears; and leave it for three more days to ensure the healing of the wounds as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, apply the instrument with gentle force according to what you did for the hair, increasing it gradually; and this is the method of hot pain, which I have written about in the treatise on rectifying medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, both in equal amounts, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If he has a small opening, make it wider with the point of a razor, and put the pot in another well-sealed pot, and pour the mixture of alkali and lime over it, stirring gently until there is a thick layer on top; leave it like this until the liquid has completely evaporated. Then take all the remaining liquid, pour it over the lime and mix it as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And thus it becomes very useful in many medical works and cautery for other limbs, as it performs the same function as fire, and with other medicines such as feverfew, aniseed, lime in soap, all these ingredients mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which a noble man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic nerve, and he says that no other remedy was done, and he was completely healed once this cure was performed, and he bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says to do this in the following way: you press and grind fresh and dry lithargy with a little fat, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and wrap it; and leave it for three hours or according to the amount that the patient no longer feels the burn.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath as long as the body is slightly aroused, and let it enter into the wound, and the pain will depart entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medications unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it provides great aid; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take some lint and grease it with old oil, and apply it to the fossa between the big toe and the one called the crescent.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking a piece of dry chamomile, heat it in the fire until it becomes ash, and place it on the cloth, leaving it until it stains; and do so again, and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it reaches the hunchback, and that the pain stops; and this method of cautery is called "chamomile cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of the severe pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain arises in the back, either from sudden impact or excessive bloodletting, or from a similar feeling of cold, expanded matter, none of these signs warrant cauterization, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient is voided of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes them on the back where the pain persists, in three lines marked with a signet, and on each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauterizations are made according to the cautery called "point"; and if you see fit, make three or four cauterizations at the median clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight and painful throat when they swallow, and fear; and you will find in the rear spine a sharp pain extending into the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe it being cured, cauterize it with the cautery iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	The cautery should own each part of the wound equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the wound with the cautery iron, piercing two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment, reset the limb as healthy according to what we have said, and beware not to apply cautery to any numb parts that are affected by a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that spreads throughout each limb, and when the pain comes on suddenly, they call it "podagra" accurately; and when it is due to a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicine, then cautery is the cure in this manner: make several cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the foot, make a cautery with what they call a "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, this happens often, so he does cautery on each knee with three or four cauterizations from each part, using olive oil; and if you need more, do so, but don't hold your hand too tightly until the expected heat is gone.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, he should administer the cautery that we have described in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two small cuts around the bones; and if there is no pain left in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part and do good governance for the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you govern it well and drain the fever, it will be healed by God's grace.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When dislocation occurs suddenly, the muscles contract and it is necessary, when you attempt to cure it, not to move the patient that day; and he should take things that ease the stomach, so that the bowels descend from his belly. After that, have him lie on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his breath until the swelling in the joints is repaired, and arrange them to your liking, and sign beneath the dislocation on the bone of the wrist, and make a mark in the shape of half a circle above the body; then take the fire according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it sheds scales.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper place; and have the attendant place his hand so they do not return to their previous position; and open the patient's thighs well, and put cushions and supports under his thighs, and another one on his pelvis which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign over your entire hand, holding it straight, and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch the bone the first time, repeat it again until you do; be careful that the bone does not move when you perform the cautery; do not burn it; and ensure the patient does not die, or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not go to the bone with cautery, your work is useless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be delicate according to their measure, and also for adults according to their size; after three days, treat the wound with butter until the scald is healed; afterwards, cure other injuries as long as they are clean, and lay the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his movements be restricted for a long time so that the boils do not appear when he moves to his room.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, a well-made bandage is applied to him and left for another forty days; and he should have good rest, working little and guarding against excessive drinking and eating, and excessive noise; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for tailoring your chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known to not grow any further, they should be treated with cautery according to their quantity, and the third of the heart should be burned; after which, follow the treatment as we have mentioned; and no one among the ancients said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the shoulder joint with a sign and draw a line across its width above the rupture, and another one behind, and hold your hand steady over the entire cautery clamp.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the initial cautery is lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, whether from a fall or an injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the application of medicine is ineffective, then it is necessary to cauterize it with a cautery called "a point," and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the member and its smallness, strength, virtue, and the location of the twist and the degree of pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is calm after the first cautery, that is good; if not, start over with another cautery on that part, because it is usual for it to move in the limb next to it, so you must perform cauteries until the patient is peaceful.
de meselerie	De meselerie" translates directly from Old French as
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These illnesses are never helped by cautery alone, especially the disease that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can treat it by cautery, taking care if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the previous division, and does not linger or delay, and you doubt that the corruption has spread throughout the patient, then make V cauterizations on the head: first on the new growth, then at the end of the hair on the forehead, next on both horns, and finally behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cauterization goes down to the bone, and as the crusts come off, let out the vapors of the thick humors so that they can drain. Treat the mouse according to what is appropriate.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the misfortune is widespread and clearly evident, then you must cauterize these cauteries that we have mentioned in the beginning, and cauterize on the spine of the nape, and cauterize on the spine of the back, and heavily cauterize on the crupie and another delicate place, and two on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of the pis, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the bottom of the feet, that you do not burn them. Never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or another on the bone of the stomach, or one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cautery, the greater the help it provides and the better the outcome; and know that the patient feels no pain from cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be deep and gentle according to the members and joints, as you will find in the manner of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, cleanse the wound with flour and honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but it remains unhealthy, then make cautery on the member according to its size and shape; and the cautery should be slightly inserted into the heart of the pain; then apply treatments until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And one should never perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the end of the nerve that causes the member to move, and thus if the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	from albars (or perhaps referring to the white part of
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical arts are of no avail, then cauterize with a hot iron according to the quantity of thick or thin cure, until the white (or perhaps referring to the affected area's color) is removed, and it changes color; then prepare a cure with flour, lentils, oil made from roses, plantain leaves, collench (or colon, possibly a type of plant), and alder bark, each in a separate part; mix them all together, wrap it in cloth, and place it on the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer appears in the beginning and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the circumference of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	However, wise people say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; nevertheless, I do not find this good, as I fear it will ulcerate and corrupt, and I have never seen it work for any patient before; and a more correct practice is to cauterize around it, in a circle-shaped cautery, as we have said regarding many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the flesh that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and they do not want to die, or because of the excessive discharge it produces, or because of the great age of the illness when it becomes debilitated (that is, too much), and there is little blood, or because of the time; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauterizations by pricking; after that, leave it alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced throughout with cautery, make sure the cautery is as hot as it should be:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	Place your hand in the middle of the disease called 'adubelati' while the cautery is pierced through the heart, and make sure the cautery is like this so that the patient feels relieved in this way that the course of the putrefaction is eliminated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, ensure it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," which is nothing but a wasting away of the members, for it wastes the members just as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a member that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery cloves both very small and very large, according to what is suitable for the member or the disease; afterward, cauterize all parts until you reach all the corruption, and leave nothing of it, so that everything that is corrupt is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply the heated cautery to the member, ground with oil, until any burning from the fire is removed, and all the corruption is healed.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds causing pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the wound does not heal, it is good; and if not, the cautery should be repeated on what has remained of the corrupted flesh.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture is sometimes cured with hot medicines instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, the fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already spoken about the treatment with cold medicines in the previous section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the liquids which come as wounds
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that a wound due to some defect arises a disease called "foul" according to our understanding, and is a large misformation which damages the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know, the cautery of fire, and the cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	For the fire cautery, take a hot iron that is also as sharp as a feather of a dove; it should be made of good iron to pierce the nail from all sides and have subtle margins; after placing the hot iron on the nail, turn your hand around the entire nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it like this for three days so that it begins to putrefy; then make a poultice of wild mallows ground with silk, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will break off and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then clean the wound with pure salt until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are moved by heat, the body's strength is often broken and many times it becomes infected in hands and feet; in such cases, it is necessary to apply cautery with hot water: take a cane of iron or bronze, or a pen of leather, and place the nail and the mold on it, that is to say, warts; then place the cane around it so that it embraces everything, and add a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning until the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and finds the hot water path deeply to the root; let the patient endure a little the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will come out at its roots entirely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have straightened all those that are in the body, then treat the wounds that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	it cures the shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone shivers from cold or quartan fever or another illness, it is necessary that you perform four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the fish, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; if this stops the trembling and hastens the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear through defects in the body's baths, or pus-filled pimples, which come from large amounts of corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it is necessary to treat them at the first appearance, one should perform a cautery on each pustule: a delicate cautery with fustic wood, of which the tip is heated in the fire, or from long aristologus root, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, nor can they grow worse in the future, but it disrupts the excesses from which they come, and heals them; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times, severe consequences arise from the blood of an artery that is cut during a wound that reaches the extreme, or during the incision of an abscess, or the cauterization of a member, and similar events; and it is very sad to experience this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Nevertheless, if this happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and stretch it out very strongly until the pain is completely alleviated from your finger, and no more blood flows; then take several small and large olive oil cauterizes, as hot as possible, and apply them to the vein until it is entirely red. Then, according to the size of the wound and the position of the artery, place the cauterize on that vein where you are holding your finger, and keep it there until the pain stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden burst of blood occurs while you are opening the vein, and the cautery is finished, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply them one after the other until the bleeding stops; be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and prevent any further harm to the patient; and know that when the blood does not subside from the artery, it cannot be properly stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either through cauterization, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly wrapping it with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and do this carefully and gradually.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief tightly binding them with cloths or placing burning objects or similar things upon them, will not be of any benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no other medicine at hand, he should place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, pressing firmly until he feels relief from the wound and the vein; and he must not move it, but moisten with cold water frequently until it becomes very cold, while the blood is congealed and thickened and relieved. And prepare in advance the things he needs for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or burning medicine, and we have discussed the applications, causes, instruments, and forms of cautery; I have placed that chapter under the primary heading up to this point, and I will proceed in this chapter along the same path for those who wish to find these things more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before I begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves more risk and danger than the first one on cautery; therefore, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who are so afraid of their illness that they die slightly because of the severity of the treatment they find for their illness, and of the greatness of their evil; of these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their consent and say: "Wait, I am bleeding"; and the illness is despicable.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not give consent to those who approach you with such behavior, but rather put more emphasis on your honor than your greed, and act prudently, not violently, with what is certain and what you can be sure of taking and letting go; and use prophecy and indication in treating your patients, so that health may be restored; and this will help you gain a good reputation, glory, and a lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most noble son, our lords grant you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering according to chapters, as it is before or the chapter of cautery, which I have devised from the beginning until the foot, so that you may find easier what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	chief filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the child's head is too tightly constrained, it causes great pain; and never does it come from a known cause as one cannot intervene.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease but in children, and to all those that I have seen, death comes quickly; and for this reason, it seems to me that I should give up the work on some treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it could not be supported; and the moisture was so great that it led to death, and this moisture gathered under the bone next to the syphac, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you make a wide cut in the head where the moisture flows; and it should be as long as necessary until the moisture goes away; and see the shape of the sponge:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deep, and the abscess greater, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the abscesses on each side of the head wide open, and there is a sharp, strong discharge when you press it with your hand from inside, and it has not healed yet, then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cuts of drapes and powders, and applying wine and oil, leave it thus for up to five days; then untie it and dress the wound with bandages and poultices, and stretch the joint evenly, and give the patient dry meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe the size of the abscess and its connection to the water, for it never appears in front or behind, nor on the right or left side.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut the abscess open and drain the water, and make an incision according to your ability; be careful not to harm the artery; then come flux of blood, so that the patient dies gently from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "cataract" either in one or both eyes, and the disease is old, and the cure with medicines does not help, then the last remedy is cauterization by cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, as soon as you have cut the arteries, make the patient raise their head; then rub the wound with a rough cloth until the arteries open; then pull the cloth firmly over the wound; then check where the vein is located, and ensure that the edges on both sides are behind the ears, and are not protruding; then mark the edges with a sign; and cut each one with a sharp spatula from two sides, reaching down to the bone, making sure to do this from the back of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatula away from the artery and cut through the clot above, cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, you must measure the quantity of space in three parts, then sign with a cross and make it bleed until the bone; and what amount of blood is to be let out is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if there is no discharge from the socket where the abscess is, dislodge the wound and bind it, and apply treatment until it heals.
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and sockets, and the pain is intense, and similar conditions have persisted for a long time, and various treatments have not helped, then we drain the arteries of the eyes and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method for extracting them is that the patient combs back the hairs from their temples and locates the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens clearly due to its pulsation, and is protected by no covering that any man who is too quick might remove; if it is uncovered, the patient gently pulls on some cloth, then rubs the area with a rough cloth, and applies hot water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the instrument in the shape of ...
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly as you come to the artery, then treat it with tweezers, and pull out the threads that adhere to each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not heal without great pain throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the vein with fire from the sixth to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two threads of strong silk so that pus does not come before the healing of the wound, and avoid complications from venom; then cut off the excess between the two threads at that very moment, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a hot iron until the joints are cut; this is the most effective treatment if the patient does not have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is help to end moisture: therefore it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the space with thick cotton and place several well-made bandages; and when they are removed, be careful to apply dry medicines that produce heat, and more bandages, as long as the wound is clean; and if you cannot find these things, immediately cover the artery with vitriol and press it with your hand so that the wound is stained; and if you do not have this at hand, place ice on the wound until it freezes, and then remove the ice with cold water as long as the wound continues to bleed, and bind it properly. The more mobile and lighter the extraction of the artery is, the better it is to cauterize the vein with this same cautery, cutting from both sides, but make sure the cuts are well spaced to maintain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they lose their warmth.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a good space, and then when you have signed with the pen the two joints, and place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and they should be spaced between the two joints because this cautery is not well fused throughout all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow down into the veins that are under the skin of the head, and no medicine applied helps, you see the face of the patient contort in pain, and feel their forehead twitch as if from a tremor; and if the eyes are red and moist, so that the paper-like membranes become detached, they are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this the "old cure for contusions", and what you do is pluck the hairs on the forehead of the patient suffering from this illness, then make three cuts on the forehead equally along its length; and one cut should extend all the way across the front, and the others two to each side of the bones beneath the skin, but be careful not to incise the arteries that are on either side of the bones. Avoid touching the area where the mandibles meet, and make sure each wound is as deep as three hairs grow in thickness; then use a piece of sponge and clean cloth to wipe away the blood, and mold it into the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple down to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two slits to all the satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision down to the other second one, and then extract this spatule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultelei" into the first slit, it should be very sharp on one side and slightly curved on the other, with this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting side towards the far edge at the heart, and the curved side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the joints, so that the incision is continuous until it opens the heart, and then make another cut in the middle, reaching the other side; then extract the blood evenly, and press the limb to remove the blood; then place a thin strip of wet cotton in each wound, and cover them with damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and lard, and ensure that no abscesses form. On the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer a strong tepid water bath, then apply basilicon treatment with rose oil, and other treatments to cure wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	your joints
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any catarrh comes that has become a habit, and you see the eyes swollen and small, weakening sight, and the mucous membranes burning; and the hair falls out, and it feels as if something is in the eye causing sharp pain, and the patient sneezes, then know from these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from a single cause, but rather from multiple veins, and the movement of the cure that is necessary.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press his forehead, then make a deep cut across the middle of the forehead, and another one very wide on the side.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, make the incision down to the bone; and move your hand away from the muscles of the temples that close when they eat. And when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood out with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton in it, and cover it with linen strips. Then wrap moist cloth soaked in wine and oil over it and be careful not to get any hot water on it; when the bone has healed, you must rub the bone until it feels hard again, then apply drying substances that cause itching.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheatflower and three parts of colophony, mix them together to make a paste, and apply it to these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear infection
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes an infection in the ears is one of four things: seeds, animals, or mineral stones or similar objects; or seed-like substances such as peas, beans, and other legumes; or flowing things like water and mud and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When the chip in the ear or any other object that does not adjust itself to the ear is stuck in the ear, it does not enter the ear, so place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a chip, distil no drop of violet oil or hyssop oil, then proceed with extraction; and it will bring up discharge from the condition, and it stops the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and raise the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, this treatment brings sudden improvement; and if it does not come out, extract it with fine tweezers, of which the shape is as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If she jumps out of the pincers, that's good; if not, perform extraction with a fine, small tool; and if she doesn't jump out, make a hook of iron and press it deep into the ear canal, sealing the wax inside so the wind cannot enter with the hook. Then treat it thoroughly, for this happens very often as we have said; if it does not come out in that way, grasp it firmly, taking care to use sharp tools, and apply a bit of cotton around it; then press the hook onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump out after trying all these things, quickly cut the ear so that the abscess hardens and stops spasming, and the cutting should be done as follows: first, prepare the patient with the appropriate treatment for cephalica, and extract the blood according to its quality. Then place the patient's ear upwards and cut a small groove at the base of the ear where the fat or cartilage is attached; make the cut in the shape of a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it carefully, and suck on the wound thoroughly with your mouth until it heals.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is stuck and swollen, then administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a thin, subtle spatula according to this form.
