et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist from earwax, as long as you have made many attempts; then extract it with thin forceps and suck gently, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water where the chunk breaks off in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use a sneezing of warm compresses first, and expand the ear with fine cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay them on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it pops out, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the pop does not come out, take many small threads according to the length of your finger, warm them slightly over fire, and insert the patient into one or more holes in their ear, from another side, and make another hole on the stone already in their ear; continue this process of thread against stone until the water comes out completely, and thus it pops out entirely. If you see any remaining threads, take another thin thread, heat one end over fire until it becomes very hot, then insert it into the ear, passing through from behind; do this several times until all the water has drained out, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of the beast, if it is of small size, like a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large and one can feel it, use pincers for its extraction; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When removing worms from the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the previous section and you are dealing with distillations, but the cure is not effective, you should examine the ear in sunlight. If no worms are visible, use very fine pincers to remove them; if they still cannot be seen, take a closer look to determine their shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be cut deeply from below and widely from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then insert the most subtle instrument into the ear according to the amount of suffering felt by the patient, then suck strongly throughout the entire canal; do this often until all the moisture is removed.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, stop up the canal with cotton as I mentioned before; and if they do not emerge as we said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat them through distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using these instruments, forming them as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a thin piece of silver or gold, cut into small points, and place it over the tiny opening to distill; and with a well-made brass instrument, press down within the distillation; then take a razor and wrap cotton around the tip carefully; pour in your oil or juice, and add whatever medicines you wish, and put the candle in the ear; then insert the razor into all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or the warmth reaches the ear; let the patient feel it within, and the distillation should be warm like when it's distilled in the ear; beware that it's not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of ear pinching
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with a perforation in their ears, and the same thing happens to adults due to ear injuries or foreign objects inside the ear; this perforation never fully heals in the ear unless one can see it; and it never becomes weak, and the hole can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the perforation appears and one cannot see it, it requires careful treatment in multiple ways. In this case, you should place the affected ear towards the sun; and examine it: if you see the hole clearly, check if there is any accumulation of wax or anything else that could be blocking it.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make incisions and cuts all around, front and back, so that the ear is not damaged; if the inflammation is from a foreign body or the cartilage of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and cut it gently until the entire cartilage is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the inflammation is deep in the ear, take a fine, sharp razor and heat it slightly over fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation in which the patient feels great pain in the ear, make a slight perforation, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the wound covered with a bandage as long as it is fresh, or take a piece of lint and moisten it in rosewater, and sprinkle vitriole powder on top; and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary to remove the lint and replace it with another moistened lint wrapped in cerate made from rosin oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it as long as it remains clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if an infection occurs, immerse a sponge and drape it in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments to remove the infection, which are treated through distillation.
de la char des papieres	Of the work of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Always consider that those that come in papers (i.e., written documents) when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to extend them with pincers and tweezers, taking care to extract the root with a spatula; then place over them vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after peeling, the cautery is done with a delicate lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision must be moved; and often they repair themselves, as no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	from the fire
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper some things that seem sleazy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a gathering of great moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: be wary if the hail mutes from one side to another, and it is a slight thing to know; then make them large, then scrape each part lightly, then take them with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it will not harm the patient; and if the split is great, and the assembly has a stitch, then cure it as long as it remains healthy; but if it is small, do not use much force, for the adhesions will restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper against it, and the pain grips in pinches, pressing from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut, drain the water and cure the swelling with salt water until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Xerophthalmia is a fat that is embedded in the films of papers above the eyes, and this occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes, and leading to cataracts in the morning, preventing them from gazing the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes. And due to this, they rest their faces downward, sleeping on them, and their papers beneath their eyebrows become moist, covered with a film that obscures and clouds the sight caused by the xerosis.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the extraction between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of performing this operation is that the patient places his head in a healthy position, then takes a linen cloth, and sets up a tent-like structure according to the quantity of extraction from each part, placing it on top; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the extraction gathers together in the middle of the circle; then, using a moistened spatula, they make a groove not wider than the wound made in the vein, and make the skin completely closed around it; and in various arrangements, more extraction comes out from the groove in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of cloth dipped in fire between your fingers and move your hand to the right and to the left as long as it is glowing; be careful not to apply it to the wound, do not reach too deep into it, do not touch the oil, do not blow on it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, gently widen the wound slightly until it opens; then take it out as we have said, and moisten cloth with water and oil, and apply it to the wound, and bind tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is stuck.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the hot abscess, treat it with external applications as long as it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows in paper (i.e., abnormally) and becomes irritated, it causes harm similar to other irritants, leading to conditions like scabs and mollifications of the skin, and albugine (a type of rash), all of which are caused by the destruction of the hair follicles; the cure is as follows: either through fire cautery, or with acute medicine according to the chapter on cautery, or through incision and stitching, or using bands, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your hand, then turn the paper from the oil on your left hand; if it rotates, that is good; if not, insert an needle through all the threads above; and take care to cut along the edge of the paper where the hairs grow out from among those hairs, and pull the thread up over the entire paper, and turn it against the razor. Then make a cut in the part below the paper, among the hairs that are close together, from the great tear all the way to the small one; then extract the thread, and place below the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and sign on the paper with a figure of an enche, like the shape of a fir tree, but it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see the paper raise up.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if from this part which has the cut, a great quantity of paper is taken according to how soft the paper is; then make a small incision along all two lines that you have marked, and begin with a large tear from one end to the other; and let it be one of the slits near the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then turn the knife in one of the two angles towards the heart, and scrape it all off; then bring together the two lips with a single stitch of a thin thread of wool, and dry up the blood, and remove the excess threads from the two edges to any sticky things, if you can do this; and if not, leave the stitching and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching using drying and constricting things, because the paper revives when the wound heals and when it is brought together, but the stitch moves (as the old ones say), and that's a work of pain; and if in another way: and this is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as if it were a pile of myrtle, as we have told it, at three points from each other according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take what surpasses small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle where there is thread, and wrap it around the figure; then take another thread from the large tear, and the smaller one from the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then gently lower your hand equally, and remove all the skin that you have marked, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and cure it until it is healed; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar ointments that relieve; sometimes the paper-like flesh is converted. It is necessary for you to use what we have said about the incision, but sewing in one way or another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for a broken arm is as follows: take paper and make it inside according to what I said, then create two arms by art, and two fine ties just as long as the paper, and tie them gently on both parts where you hold the bones; then assemble one onto the other delicately over the paper from oil, and pull the two arms from the formed parts; leave it like this for several days, and the flesh that was restrained will die and wither until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed and the wound has gathered strength, then treat it as long as it remains healthy; and if the paper is dried, and the hair does not grow back, and the bones have healed, then make the two arms according to this figure and this measurement of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves piercing the skin with a fine needle and threading it with soft, thin silk thread; then joining the edges and tying them gently, making the length of the threads one palm's length. Next, arrange another thin silk thread swiftly and tie the ends tightly. Place the patient's head in your hands, and gently perform the procedure, declaring the work done since it is a delicate and minute task. Then, insert the needle throughout the entire wound at the root of the hair, carefully piercing the paper until you remove it from the natural skin; then pull out the hair up to the wound in the paper, and thread the hair back into the wound if there are one, two, three, or more hairs; finally, withdraw your hand when the hairs have completely detached from the wound in the paper with the natural skin.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, pull the wound from the inside to the outside along all the thread you have threaded, until the wound comes out completely and you see through the eye of the needle; then pull the wound and the thread, close the eye and leave it for one or two days, until the hair grows back in its place and the scar heals. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural horsehair, and let it grow with the one you leave, until it becomes elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurity of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes about in the body, it has two causes: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from wounds, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of performing this operation is that you cut open the wound, separate the lips, and insert pieces of linen, binding them until the wound is healed; and it is not advisable to use drying or constricting substances in the treatment of such things.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it works through softening agents, such as fenugreek; and rosewater of water or oil, and flaxseed are cooked, and garlic dissolved in any of the eyes, and it wraps around a bandage, and the cure for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true power of your cure lies in ensuring it does not harden according to its previous form; and this work that we have spoken of is only a remedy for this illness, so that it does not return according to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the grease that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is the separation of joints, is truly called "arthritis," and it is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from wounds, cracks, cauterization, and similar things; and the result of the work in this case is such that if you pierce a needle with two strands and insert it into the flesh, it should go through both sides, so that the threads come out on either side of the wound; then the flesh swells over the needle, and the skin around it becomes large.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the shape of the paper returns to what is appropriate, that is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the crack, turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side of the incision; let the edges of these cuts form two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are brought together, the shape resembles the curve of a letter with a lower case 'g'; then remove the paper, according to the thickness of its sides, from what is left over, and adjust the two irregular parts by stitching them with a thread of wool; finally, apply the treatments we have mentioned for softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from cutting, stitching, or cauterizing, it is necessary that you make a clean cut beneath the skin among the hairs, and according to what has been said before; then separate the two halves of a single wound, as I have mentioned; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled masters devise various instruments to restore the natural shape, and the patients themselves, according to what is appropriate for the work and the tools in different arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	Dislocation" is the most probable translation for "dou soudement de la papi
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture is done in the usual manner that the paper on top is smooth with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor beneath the paper and lift it gently; and hold it like pincers until you remove what is sharp on the delicate spatula, which should not be too acute or too harsh, so that the patient does not suffer from the excessive sharpness of the spatula; and make your incision, by scraping together the gathered paper, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all the gathered paper becomes healthy, and there is no saltiness in the oil, nor any bitterness, and raise it with sweet water and a collar. Then place between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on top of the oil moist wool in abundance; and after the third day use a collar and things that soften until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail has two types of appearances: it is either nervy and resembles a hard, dry tissue, or it is not nervy but appears as white, moistened congealed matter, which, when touched with iron and treated with pincers, cannot be moved; and both resemble the beginning of the great toe, growing little by little until it covers the entire sight, all the light, and the movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The procedure for incision is as follows: the patient places his head on a healthy surface, then opens the fingers; takes a piece of paper in their hand, then coils the nail with small pincers, extending it upwards; takes an needle, threads it with horsehair, goat hair, or oxen hair, and a strong thread; doubles the needle's point and pierces it through the nail, all the way to the tip, and ties the nail with the thread, extending it upwards, and shaves off all the hair around the nail, starting from the base towards the top, using a sharp blade; then shapes the remaining part at the root of the finger, with a delicate and small force, leaving the natural shape of the nail or finger. In no case should the nail be extended immediately after cutting; it should only be done with thread as we have said. Then, the shape takes on this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the scalpel does not touch and tear the soft flesh, and that the cut is not too deep; afterward, pour a little of the ground silk into the wound and add some collyrium made from lithargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not connected to a nerve and you cannot push the needle, and the hooks cannot enter, this type of fingernail is often treated with medicine; as I have described in detail. If you see it covered, open the wound gently for the patient and take a light scalpel following this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gently from above, and if you see that it shrinks little by little and the reason hastens, then let it drop into your mouth from a collar made of collyrium (a medicinal ointment) and a red string, and stop the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If any substance in the oil is contrary to you, such as a hot abscess, then cool it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is completely cured.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh in the eye causes harm in oil by great damage, suspending it at an angle, and cutting off a part but not all, no tears will come; then a red collyre is distilled in the oil, which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	on the flesh that is born on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people are born without any red flesh on the iris, covering and restraining it with threads and strings, making it appear like a rose petal; and this is so that the patient places his head in a healthy position, then opens the eyes, and carefully removes all of the affected flesh using appropriate tools, supporting it with force. Then, cut the first piece, going around completely until the end, taking care not to damage the eye during the operation. And use the oil from crushed seeds or distill a red collyre and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton soaked in hot oil on the affected area; be sure that the abscess is hot. If nothing remains, and there is no pus, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for a hot abscess. Then return to your work as long as it remains healthy, and thus make all other cuts in the eye following this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you attend to the care of each weak oil in the natural way; and in the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not thrust your hand into any of these works until you see that this member suffers from this work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are the red veins that are covered over the eye, they steal from the sight its work and weaken the eye every day.

Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then gently pull the veins, wiping off the blood hour after hour, until you remove the veins from the flesh; and be careful not to pierce the oil with the points of the forceps, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your task so that you do not leave any veins behind; and when you have done this, distil green and red collyrium into the oil to corrupt what remains in the sebaceous glands.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of them in that hour, make a poultice over the wound with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for no more than a day until the pain is eased and the hot abscess is assured, then continue according to this manner as long as it is healthy; and this is the form of the veins:
de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He calls these fistulas "arissati": when you treat them with cautery and strong medicine as I have said above, and they are not healed, there is a cause within that you must cut into the abscess, where he will die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the tools mentioned here and shape them; it is called "the sharp edge", and it should be made from iron from the tip to the handle, and pointed like a file as shown in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone back in its position, then twist it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the joint with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joints are fused and the patient is born that way, and the bowel's core is also fused and remains so for 40 days without renewal or abscess formation, and no bad accidents occur, then it is healthy; if not, there is another tool to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and aguë medicines, and when it is uncovered, take care for it as shown here, and let the iron be at three angles, and the pointed part should be thinned as you see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the clean bone of the arm, remove your hand from the blood, and go through with all the treatment until it pierces the bone and the patient feels relief because the pain goes away if he keeps his hand on his nipple; and afterward, return to the use of dry remedies, as I have taught you, and when the swelling and hardness of the bones subside, examine the nipple; if it becomes lighter, then it is a milder case for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the wound
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is completely open and does not disturb or shrink the nipple, it is necessary to keep the patient; then apply poultices or sucking cups without hurting, and pour oil made from aloe, frankincense, and myrrh onto it, and then strain the oil, and put the paste on bandages and cloth; and the way of arranging the cloth should be that you make each layer soft and double them in four, and place one over the other according to the need of the wound; then strain it from above with a firm, formless bandage, and continue with the cups for sucking without hurting; then remove the cups and leave the paste strained for a day and night, and if it becomes soft, it is good; if not, repeat the poultices, cloth, paste, and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	breakage of the skin's surface
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the skin's surface, it opens and lets out small bits like grains of resin, which is somewhat reassuring to see; then, if you notice this, the work involves inserting an needle into the base of the affected area, just above its root, and then another needle where there is a double thread from the damaged part towards the edge. You pierce it, leaving the first needle in place, then cut the double thread and tie a piece of cloth around it tightly. Afterward, you remove the needle and apply fresh, moist lint to the wound until the thread separates from the skin, and you repeat this process for each section until the wound is healed. In no case should the wound be restricted by the cloth in any circular pattern while it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the joint has a great appearance, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from oil, and remove the white moisture and lower the joint, then insert it again as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the vein (or artery)
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not acute (sudden), but seems to be a steady flow (like a vein), and it is not a true flow; and the manner of performing this operation is as follows: place the patient in an upright position, then take hold of the head with both hands from either side, and move it until you see the vein rising towards your fingers. Then press it firmly, and if the blood does not flow down, know that it is a true venous condition, and if the pressure allows, release it as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient rest between your hands, then take the delicate spatula and make incisions in the corneal membrane along with the conjunctiva connected to the corneal membrane and the crown, until the bowel is released; and when it is released, it distills into hot clear oil mixed with honey, or boiling fennel seed and honey, then apply another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	des aiges de l'oil" translates directly to "of the waters of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar waters in division, and what should be pierced; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should place the patient between your crossed hands away from direct sunlight and tie a healthy cloth tightly around them; then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the limbs are on the left side, or in your right hand for right-sided limbs; next, take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the limbs are on the left, or in your left hand for right-sided limbs; then place the tip of the instrument along the thickness of a single strand at the outer edge of the oil's bleached area, and press the instrument called "almagda" firmly, feeling as it enters the bleached part of the oil; and ensure the measure of the almagda is equal to the entire space from the prunelet to the end of the darkness; this is the oil's corona. You will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the corned cloth, then place the instrument up to where the water begins, and press it along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he sinks deeply now, then the patient must see the ill person before him and hold the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, he sinks down again the second time, inserts the instrument and when it is firmly in place and does not move up, gently extract the maggots by turning your hand back and forth; then dip again in clear oil and remove from that oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place the hot oil or any other moistened oil in a robed and abundant container, and tie it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply a fine flour with much heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the mixture cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many individuals with very hard eyelids, it is necessary that you press the instrument called 'alberit', which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva gently, and do not cut too deeply, but make it subtle, then inject the mixture as we have said; and after the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep with a comfortable position, on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and feed him light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition until the third day. Then release him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see any objects, and then put on the bandage again for seven days; and it is not appropriate that you perform this at the time of treatment or after incision now, but you should lighten it, because acute pain rises dangerously.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; when it is soothed, loosen the bandage and place a small roll on its face to cover it for some time, and then return to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little and return to its former state; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then came to us one from the East who told us of a certain plant that, in its native land, is used to draw out water, but I had never heard of it in our country nor read of it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of magic, because whoever does not know them will see them as different; and they should be of pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the top of this same subtlety be in the center, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the edge
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No one should ever give birth to or have any children with diverse aligned charms, from which there are none that seem like scorpions due to their abundance of joints; and if such exist, the charm is enchanting in its bright color, and the child is smooth with a good appearance.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the bone is soft and not yet healed, you must make the patient lie between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, apply the knife to those parts, and treat them fiercely; cut what you can hold with the delicate blade from one side, until you know that the bone is completely separated.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, cut it open with all the delicate and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and without hesitation, perform the incision as necessary; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize until the blood is dried and all bones are separated. Then apply ice and water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out until the gums are clean, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is something stuck in the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, and be careful with your hands, and leave between each a space no larger or smaller than necessary; and put the patient's tooth into the thread at his ability, and pull it out while smelling until it comes through the gum inside the mouth; and often children do so in school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it. Then hold the gum that comes through the mouth with one hand, and the other gum that comes through the mouth with the other hand, knowing one after the other as we are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, corrupt the wound with new tissue, then treat the son, wipe away the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has healed all that remains of the wound; and then place a bandage around the head for no more than a day, if it is healthy, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, and use it thus; if you see, make a closed pipe, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have many at hand for the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, a sickness near the nose arises, which is called "telul," and it grows large and becomes extremely painful, such that it is a sight to behold. Therefore, it is necessary that you handle it at the beginning, remove all the flesh, then apply hot cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in covering it until it becomes large, be careful if it hardens, takes on a dark color, or lacks sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscessed joint, because when you cover it, great harm comes to the patient. If the abscess is sensitive, not dark-colored, and you are able to completely cover it without pain, empty the patient and cover it without delay, using dry and restrictive things for the cure.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	as soon as the wound is cut and dressed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the fluid from a joint leaks out into one of these strong cartilage tissues, it benefits no one, except perhaps no one at all.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore important that no one touch where the injury is fresh; then sew the two edges together and treat it until it heals; and if the lips have already separated from each other, you should scrape all parts of their core while they are healing, then sew the two lips together, tighten them, and apply a mixture of dragon's blood powder and incense dust; and place a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster on the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat with care until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring together the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips become hard, resembling small grains, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips and make a cut under each one, taking them as pincers and grinding them in each part; then apply the vitriole after the incision, until the wound is stained; then use the dry leaf, and cure the wound with moist things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the disease of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a disease of the gums called "albulus" arises, and it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, cut it at its root, and let the blood or pus flow out; then apply powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders over it. If the gum returns after the incision, this often happens a second time, and cauterization should be performed; if it does not return after cauterization, these are the shapes of the tools used to cut.
des sordens	from congestion
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth should be assembled at the top of the gums, within the mouth between the teeth and gum tissues, which are unattractive and rough; no tooth should be black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption reaches the gum, and they stink; it is necessary that you make the patient hold still in your hands, and his teeth or gum tissue exposed in your safe place, until nothing remains; and do this with blackness and verdigris and jaundice and other conditions, until they are clean; and if what is at the first cause is removed, it is good; if not, recommence on the second day and third, until everything is cut; and know that teeth require various tools to cut them, according to what the work demonstrates, because the cutter used to remove teeth from between them has other shapes than that which cuts them within. And these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you do not delay drawing it out as much as possible, for no one should do so; for it is a very precious substance, and one has no excuse to neglect it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained from drawing out the tooth, it is necessary that you be certain of the painful tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient feels pain, believing that a tooth is infected, and has it drawn out; however, the pain does not leave until the abscess is extracted, as we have seen with these patients; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, it is necessary to scrape around the tooth with a sharp spoon to protect the gums from all sides. Then move the pliers bit by bit with your fingers or use fine tweezers at the first poke and poke, until they are well wedged, then firmly hold the pliers; and place the patient's cheek between your knees, holding it there so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and press gently from every side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and chipped, it is necessary to fill the gap with cloth, either from the opening or the perforation; and if it is tightly stuck with pliers, be careful not to break it while pulling; and it is very important to work gently around the gums to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return to the patient, as the evil of the root causes greater pain than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, through their haste and boldness, often break the vessels, and fail to take heed of what we have recounted; but they bring about great illness through their words, either because of the roots where they dwell, or because of the vessels that they break, as we have often seen. And when there is bleeding, wash the wound with wine or ash and silk; and if this does not stop it, apply vitriol; and if that fails, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one first mute the bleeding, should be long and thick-handed, not doubling over as you draw out the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the members be of good size so that they do not bend when pulled, and made of iron well-forged, and toothed for holding fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root persists when pulled, it is necessary to place a cotton ball moistened with butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the limbs are relaxed, then use pliers called 'algefri' to gently extract them, making them look well-cared for; and they should be shaped like a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not emerge from these grips, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is a file, of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is hard and thick so that it does not break, and the root jumps out by itself, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, whose shapes are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two edges, its shape is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are used in the treatment of teeth, and this tool that seems like large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This tool should be robust so it does not break, and you should know that many dental tools exist; there are also other tools, which are not mentioned.
