The most skilled surgeons invent their own instruments, according to what their work and the illness show them, because there are certain diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients. If a part breaks or becomes stuck in another bone, or if it is difficult to extract, and he seeks the appropriate instruments I have mentioned, and uses gestures to guide him, this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-joined to hold the bone firmly, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the limb to suitable medicine, and if there is decay in the bone, even if it is small, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the permanent one and is not in the right position, and it cannot be cut or filed; then extract it. And if it is mobile with the tooth, take this instrument whose form resembles a small beak, and let it be sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the dentist should hold it with his hands day and night for the pain in his teeth, and because you cannot move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as its shape is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also similar to how they file the points of needles; file the tooth gently with your fingers day and night until it stops moving, then in the end, it should be completely smooth, without any roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it is necessary to file away the rough spots until it is even so that it does not hurt the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches strongly, either from impact or biting, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, they only experience pain when touched, and medicines applied do not help. Then they should be restrained with a gold thread, for silver wire turns green and decays, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you successfully align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth next to the painful one, then place the gum tissue between the smaller teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; continue wrapping the thread tightly, carefully and painfully, until it does not move. And the root of the aching tooth should be held firmly so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the fragments of bone with pliers, assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that the tongue does not bleed; and leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, the threads will unravel, as if pulled by another thread. It should remain in this position for as long as possible, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy incisors and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is reset in its place, freshening it as we have said; and let no one intervene unless they are skilled and patient, and never form a tooth from a bone of a weak animal, but place it where the defect lies, pulling it tight as we have said, and holding it for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut open the tongue's surface.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what kind of wound this comes from, whether it's natural or caused by a deep cut; and if it's due to an accidental deep wound; the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with care, keeping their head in a safe position, and gently pulling out the tongue; then cutting the nerve's connection with a wide cut, as much as possible, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is any stiffness or hardness, and it's a sudden deep wound, use a hook and make a wide cut of that ligament; be careful not to sever the artery located below; after finishing, raise the affected area with rosewater or cold water, then apply a linen bandage over the tongue; and keep doing this every night so that the tendons do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the fever comes from an infection, put a hot poultice on it; and if the pain intensifies, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for healing; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is red or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it becomes pale and there is moisture, drain it with a fine needle, and dig out its veins, and free it on both sides; and if the pain persists in your work, apply a hot poultice as long as it is stained, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly. Then lift the limb gently and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No symptom ever occurs within the throat that are called "godath", and they are properly known as the two amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not well healed, be careful: these apostemes are hard to discern by their small size and pale color, so do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also because of the flow of blood; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own; and if they are of a white color again, and the root is thin, have a ready instrument to cover, but first ensure that the aposteme cools down and calms down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and keep his feet in good condition, open his mouth wide, and press the tongue down with the instrument, so that it takes the shape of it; and use silver or fine gold, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue to all of this instrument and see the abscess, so take the hook and the file and insert them into it, pulling upwards as much as possible; do not touch any part of the strings with it, then cut with the instrument, forming a shape that looks like teeth; nevertheless, the tip is curved, one side faces another, and they are very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pliers, in this way:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be pierced from one side and named; and when you have extracted one of the stones, extract the other in the same manner; then, after incision, gargle the patient with hot water mixed with vinegar and salt, or with pomegranate peel, or mullein leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then apply the cure while it is still fresh; and no other abscesses will form in the throat besides these two stones, if they are extracted in this way as with the two stones.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was located inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and I had closed the entire throat tightly, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained in that state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through both openings in the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a needle into one of the openings and pulled it through, then withdrew it again and took out a large portion of pus; I did the same in the other opening, opening the mouth and pressing on the tongue. After inserting the needle into these abscesses and draining some of the pus, only a little blood came out; thus, the passageway in the throat was opened for her to begin drinking water and then wine, and I continued to drain the abscess for a long time. The abscess recurred again, filling the space that I had emptied, becoming very large. Then I bandaged it and cauterized it inside the throat; in this way, it healed without increasing. And I left these treatments, and only God knows what happened afterward.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina descends to the eye, and it is swollen and extended, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is detached, thick, and rounded, it is called "retina".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess has healed, and it is small, it is necessary to drain it; and the one that is rounded and not extended too much; and it is red or of a dark color, it is advisable to avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the poor patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, take the patient's tongue with your fingers and press it with the instrument we spoke of before; then insert the needle into the eye, remove it from the back, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in making the incision on the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is important that you do not cut off any excess beyond the natural limit, for if you do, it will be painful to speak and move; after the incision, use what we said regarding the incision on the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from great pain, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterization to alleviate the painful sensation.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very sharp and acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head on a healthy surface and then press their tongue with the instrument mentioned in this chapter (cauterization), using it gently but firmly, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and when using this instrument, follow its shape as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the physician have a fine brush, as if for stirring a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and have the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus from his mouth carry the medicine down, preventing it from going to the throat and causing pain; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it cease and the pain from the medicine subside; and if you observe, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument completely into the cloth on top of the eye, until the cotton adheres to the eye; do this often until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, or even five, if you need to repeat the cauterization, repeat it, and after the cauterization, wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; then rinse with cold water and use gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cauterization, especially through incision; if it is performed by fumigation in this manner, take mullein and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and combine them all or any of them in a pot, and put it on the fire; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and among the pot place a cheveit (a type of instrument) as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes numb; afterward, it often recurs until the eye dries up, and beware not to perform this at the onset of a hot abscess, as many complications arise; and do not attempt this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and insert within the mouth a piece of cold wool, so that it does not burn the patient's mouth; for the piece of wool does not allow the heat to weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a sharp bone or a fish spine or any such thing gets stuck in the throat; so you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, until you see the object move; and if it doesn't open and is lodged in the throat, make the patient vomit so that the food in their stomach is cooked; perhaps this will dislodge the object through vomiting. Or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval bone, or a lettuce root, or a crust of dry bread; tie a string to the sponge and then pull it out; and when it reaches its place, it will come out, and then you can extract it further. If none of these methods work as described, take an instrument made of pure salt according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And take the hooked instrument to the throat so that it can enter more easily, and raise the head, and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest all the phlegm come back, and do not push the bone inside; and let the patient force the instrument, because it needs to move in order for the thing to clear; if it goes down, draw it out evenly throughout the entire instrument, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	regarding the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I said in the previous section, except with medicinal remedies; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, take it to the smallest pin or fine tweezers that are suitable for it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if these tools are not suitable, take a horsehair strand, and insert it into the throat of the patient with the wound, then pull it out or gently warm it, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in, letting him swallow it, and do this often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and infuses the patient with bad smell from the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you light a pot with hot coals and place a perforated cover over it to contain the smoke. The patient then puts the end of the pipe in their mouth, sealing their lips so that the smoke does not escape, but instead fills their nose. The smoke should now clear, and if it doesn't, repeat the process several times. The patient should endure thirst and eat salty and bitter foods without drinking water, until the discharge runs clear through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it can be seen, resembles curved pincers for entering the throat; and it looks like a hawk's beak, and has the roughness of stone, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot let go; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the knowledge that comes from this book, both in terms of perforation and incision; and they differ in two ways, one being in their same appearance, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is through the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess has a different nature from that of the base, and the abscess of the flesh is different from that which comes in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if at abscesses one must not pierce until the bowel is dead according to its completion; and if of such as it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and they are left until the pus is surrounded, it may corrupt the ligaments and nerves of the joint, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member and you delay puncturing it until it becomes gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; or if it is in the foundation, you should puncture it likewise so that it does not become gangrenous, but instead stays open, forming a fistula, and cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforating an abscess that is deadly according to its completion; this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness lessen, and the swelling of the abscess's head diminishes, and other signs appear; and it is necessary that you make the perforation depend on the location of the abscess, where it moves most; and the perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and tendons and arteries, or anywhere without fluid.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fatty part of the body, it is better to let the incision heal completely before moving it, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before the abscess has formed, the body's defense will push the pus out, and it will be filled with much filth; and by chance, the lips might harden and sink into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the thick part of the body, as needed for the limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat them with small incisions, small openings; and in large ones, large openings and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to dig out the heart and cover it; when it has become as hard as a blanket and is numbed, then it should be treated like boils: and if they are cut in three angles, or such that one covers them like a sheet of mirth, like the abscesses of attackers; and if there are such where one makes a round-sized, or other-sized cuts, and similar openings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like a painful superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it deeply; and if the abscess is large, and it has a great bowel attached, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bowel at once, but a part of it. Then stop the abscess until the next day, and afterwards do not touch it again; repeat this many times, gradually, until the bowel comes out entirely; especially if the patient is weak in constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or old, frail people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often hope jumps with the outcome of the bow, that by chance it kills the patient, and you will not persist.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound is clean, and the abscess wound is small; and if it is a deep wound, apply either linen or cotton cloth; and if it is a large abscess with much opening, then attach a tent to each so that they come together; and if you have in the abscess a part of hard skin, and you have cured it around, then fill it with old cotton or linen raspings without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it and apply the cure as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and ice, and moisten the bandage, and place it over the bleeding wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply government and treatment, and the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is a deep wound or an abscess, it is necessary to place these and damp cloths with wine and hot oil; and if it is in such a state, and the wound is fleshy, then place moistened cloths with cold water and fresh oil, or wine and hot oil, for up to three days, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and clean and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have already told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is that chapter.
des soros	from sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there often appear small abscesses, which are like threads, also like the stitches of a woman's dress, and they have many similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are thick and have moisture, as well as pulsating; and if there are such that are hard and difficult to cut, then there is no doubt that the arteries do not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the body if such that you should try all instrument called "instrument of insertion", from which comes the form below, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make an opening from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, if it cuts off nothing, leaving the skin that contains the moisture, then it returns repeatedly once you leave it alone; then dip a cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, use water and string, and apply to the wound, and leave until the next day; and this will heal those who are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second and third days, as long as you know that it does not stay in place at night; then treat the wound with suitable care until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess is large, follow this form: cut deeply; drain the pus from all sides, and apply all your care to extract it from the cloth where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Also do with an abscess that is deep, cutting and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess and the moist flesh first, for it has less blood because they are small wounds.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if none of these abscesses or boils have any moisture, and among these hard abscesses that I found on the head of an old woman, I discovered one as hard as a stone, sharp and white, and unbreakable; and if anyone were to try to break it, they would do no less harm than with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that occur on the head, especially those that come at the top of the head or at the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept completely open for as long as possible to allow the pus to drain; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and it dissolves the adhesions, and inflames the surrounding parts, and never comes elsewhere on the body, and it is painful, and tightly twisted with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is strictly within its rib, as we have said of the nodule and abscess in the head, and there are many appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are evil and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see with good disposition for touch, and it resembles the color of healthy flesh, and is quiet from every side, and has no openings as the nerve in the collar or the artery or the channel, and is not too deep; then you should cut through it from above, and peel from every part, and the two lips of the heart be where they are supposed to be, if needed, as we have said in chapters about the head; and proceed little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make them too sharp so that your hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriole (a corrosive substance) or any powder that stops blood flow, and close the wound; leave it until the inflammation subsides, and the wound softens, and then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work until you complete it; then pay attention to your expert indication if there remain no small bumps, if you dry and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the bump, it is not enough that you remove only the bump at its root, but tie it with a double strand of strong thread and leave it hanging without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire bump, it is necessary that you close both lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no excess due to the size of the bump.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand how to deal with the root of it, and pull it out forcefully, then cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have an excess, open them where they appear to be most infected; and treat them in the same way as those previously mentioned, depending on the condition, then apply these remedies with cleaning and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is left from the corruption; and once the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment until it is cured.
de squinance	squinance (Old French) = squint (Modern
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They (the ancients) spoke and wrote about the anatomy of the throat; but I never saw in our land anyone who performed it, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint (strabismus), it is important to avoid the throat's fold, called the epiglottis; for this condition does not improve with help, as all the veins and the pores of the sick person are close to each other in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the urinary channel, it is important to cover the epiglottis to prevent the damage caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles or according to the size of the cut, without touching the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no charring, and the edges remain long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he extends the throat skin completely around the circle, then cuts the heart until it reaches the trachea; and avoid blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syphilis as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the river of the trachea that jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound near the heart, and cut through them entirely where the cartilage is; then administer medicines that induce heat until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim warns that this should not be done until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is deemed to be at death's door, with no hope of recovery.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then they should cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients ordered the wound to remain open until the evil of the disease has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded that the wound be sutured and treated, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel was wounded by a knife, and she stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the tongue from the jaw; and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it; I realized that she had no strength or control over her voice, and the wind came out through the wound in her throat.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and after she had regained her voice, she returned to her senses; for this reason, I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "throat hernias", and they are large abscesses in the color of a jet, and they occur mostly in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental, or without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners: one is like fat, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from the artery; it causes fear, and one should not attempt to make cuts except in the case of a small abscess, and test and examine all entries: if you find it similar to fat and cannot be moved in any way, treat it as you would treat a nosebleed, and remove all foreign bodies if present; then wrap it well and cure it as appropriate until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we can approach this, of which I will describe all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the entire distinction between us and our origin.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that origin is heat and fever holding, as long as the boiling is not complete, and then ends the putrefaction; after that, the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new birth, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac and according to the state of the body, and begins like a seed, and becomes large; and are according to two appearances, either fat or moist, and much of color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you approach the treatment of a new case, first test and inquire about every instrument called "forceps", according to its shape, in this chapter or the next.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is to press more or less moistfully on the abscess, and move your fingers in and out little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the core; then do this according to the size of the abscess; then extract the forceps, and be careful not to let it slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture is running through the wound, what color it has, do as I said for other abscesses; and if the forceps does not become moist afterward, know that it is dry, so cross it with the pincers and gently scrape each side, and take care of the skin where it lies, pulling it out until it becomes healthy again with the new; and if you cannot pull it out healthy, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not stay, it returns to the mind many times; and if it delays a little, without disturbing you, it employs the wound with various corrosive powders and remedies, tightens the wound, applies hot poultices and treats it with other remedies until it is healed; and when it is grave, it costs both lips of the wound and treats those who cause it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the veins are hardened against it or any other thing hurries you, use the vitriol powder and leave it for two or three days until the wound purifies itself and rests from the blood flow; then return to cover what has fallen away again.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments that enter, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters called 'albaret' and one called 'breb', and these are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas; and they are similar to needles with which sorceries are cut, and are made of gold, tin, or iron, and those that are yellow are more effective for enclosing the black cores of fistulas; and these are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the extent of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and also there are hooks with two prongs in three ways; and hooks with three prongs, also in three ways; and hooks with two prongs, and sometimes a single-pronged hook, in three ways; all these are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut well enough on one side, leaving the skin uncut, for they do not sever the vein or nerve; and from such insertions come the alemes, which are placed in parts, so that the patient does not suffer when opening the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use them only on fleshy parts, like legs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places; and never make another small tool, resembling the cuts of fists, according to this form, with which one stops the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that heals the severing of veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as they seem like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them should do so according to this form from this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal poultices with hot char to the wound, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healthy; if the breast sinks downwards and becomes soft due to its size, as it does in women, making two incisions above, through two similar openings; so that one holds onto the other at the end of each, ensuring that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from this line b until g. Then scrape off the leather between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, until it is healed; and if it does not heal, or the incision is not entirely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood discharge, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing, and leave it until it removes the remaining fat and tissue, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply a wound dressing of clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then treat it as we have said for cuts in scrofula, and if the wound gapes open, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sealed, it often leads to abscesses, and similarly occurs in a vein that is inflated and abscessed; and if one knows this is due to an artery, then the abscess should be left to heal on its own; and when you feel it in your limbs, it feels strange; and for a vein, it appears red and swollen; and it is foolish to try to drain this abscess, especially when it is deep within joints or infected with angers (angrines) or in the collarbone or other parts, as it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and the one at the head should also beware, and for that which is close to an artery's surface, make a cut from above the skin long; then carefully open the wound as often as necessary, and remove the artery with a single thread in two parts, just as I taught you regarding the extraction of both arteries found within temples. Then mark the space between the two threads with an instrument until no pus remains, and treat the abscess. Then apply the cure as appropriate while the wound is open; tend to any ensuing care as needed, so long as it is healthy. If the abscess lies along a vein's cut, you should hold in your hand what you can of the abscess, then insert the needle from below the space you hold, and pierce it, making two threads, so that you draw it from the other side; then secure the abscess as I instructed, or tie it to one of its parts with a thread. If you doubt that the thread has come loose, reinsert another needle throughout all of the abscess, below where the first was inserted, and draw out the threads in four parts. Then cut off the excess part of the abscess, and cut away any remaining surplus from the skin; leave what remains attached. Then place a moist cloth made of wine and oil upon it, and apply treatments and remedies as needed until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscesses of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, abscesses also form in nails when they are injured or subjected to excessive strain, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in joints and fingers, which is the cause of abscesses, and their appearance resembles the color of the skin, and they are in various dispositions causing pain; and when they form, the patient feels great pain, and it is not fully integrated into the body, but deviates towards the heart; and it moves from all sides, neither advancing nor retreating, upwards or downwards, and the joint that is affected should not be bound with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and the one located at the head or forehead, makes the skin split.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it has a claw-like shape, cut it at its base; and if it's large, suspend it with a hook, then scrape off the skin, and later clean and stitch the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates from Old French to "hanging large
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It happens in bellies alone, and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to its appearance, it has subtle roots, and large droppings; there are both small and very large ones. I have seen people with two or more such growths in their bellies that looked more like fungi than anything else, with no discernible difference, they were white, had fine roots, were deeply split, and constantly discharged moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I collected and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 З., and the work of the incision is such that you look at the patient's moistness, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if it cuts with a wide spatula, then perform fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often brings too much blood loss, and if it bleeds heavily without stopping, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient anxious and fearful of the incision, take a well-made plunger and bind the artery as we have said, leaving it for two days; then restrain it and do not cease to tighten the plunger until it cuts through the artery without effort; and if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut, especially in the abdomen, but you can still cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not bleed again; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the thin part which is red, poor in substance, and milky-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound comes from cauterization of a wound or a fissure in the flesh, and it is on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as it often happens with other ruptures, or from blood letting from veins or arteries according to what is above, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the rupture through the flesh and the discharge of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed at its two ends, it bends back and then returns, and perhaps it narrows or widens at the entrance of the bath or because of hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter and opens easily when pressed in the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: large and hard abscesses, fixed in quantity; and if it is due to wind, it feels soft to the touch, and the work involves observing whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be an intestinal or bowel problem, you must instruct the patient to keep their bowels motionless and straight, then stitch around it; then command them to shift it gently between your hands, then stretch the part of the abscess above all the large sinew; then tie it with a strong thread or firm silk string, making it immobile; then open the other half of the abscess that is stretched over the string and use your finger to explore; if you find it caught in the string, release it and bring the intestine out from inside the belly; and if you find the bowels, take them at the sinew, cut off the surplusage; and if the artery or vein causes trouble, gently go around it; then return to your work and take two needles, push them through with force, and stitch as you did when making the incision; then stretch the abscess three times on the needles, and if you see it receding, remove the needles, leave the wound to heal on its own, and cure the patient as necessary; then remove the blood or moisture you find, cure the wound appropriately, and finish the abscess as we have said.
dou chancre	A cancerous ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the symptoms of cancer and how to treat it with medicines, as well as how to avoid iron treatments; we say that cancer is insidious in the body, requiring great caution in its treatment, and advise the ancients that when a cancer can be cut out, like one on the breast, or the thigh, or similar places, it should all be removed as soon as possible.
