And when it is large and old, you should not even approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for tasks where the cancer is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, you should never purge the patient of black blood; instead, make them healthier if there is obvious congestion, then operate to remove the cancer from its good place; then pour on the cancer and all its parts, and cut it from all sides, leaving nothing behind; let the blood flow out completely, and check the wound with your hand or any other object, and if the bleeding continues after the cauterization of the artery or vein, you should continue to cauterize until the blood stops; then apply another cure as long as it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsis 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the signs of hydrops, and in what way the collection of fluid is formed, and the symptoms of each condition, and the cure using medicines, and that which is cured with iron; these two conditions are the only ones to be considered. And one should not apply iron to these two conditions: namely, tympanitis and ypocrates, for they are deadly; so when you treat this hydrops-like condition, called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not benefit the patient, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydrops, such as a stomachache, or similar conditions. Do not apply iron in these cases, for there is doubt; but if you see that the patient is of strong constitution, and suffers only from hydrops, and is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lay the patient gently on your hands, and the attendant should press the abdomen towards the bottom, squeezing out the fluid to the lowest point, then take the sharp spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pierce with a point, but do not insert it so deeply that it reaches the intestines when pushed in, and do not let it pierce through; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. You should make your incision three fingers' width directly beneath the armpit on the side where the droop occurs. If the drooping is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the armpit; and if it's due to a weak muscle, make it on the right, so that the patient does not lie on the incision, allowing excess fluid to drain from the weak joint. Then, with the instrument, pierce through all the skin and flesh, and push it out, and apply pressure to any pus or debris between the skin and the affected area, as if you were peeling a wound open with your fingernail or similar; then continue piercing until the pus reaches the eighth 'leu', which is the color of water, then pull out the instrument, and shape it as shown:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of fine gold or silver, with one small opening in the middle, and on one side three openings, and on the other two, and one on the other; and the part is cut as if it were a feather, which is the shape of the incision that scribes make to cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it, there is a membrane, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends upon the instrument; then empty half or a third, for if you empty more than is necessary at this time, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit into the weapon, or he may lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient indicate, and his pulses. Then take the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the core that stops the opening which I mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this for one day, and be careful not to let it remain too long but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, either by burial or hot sand, or by sweating or a bath, or in the sun, and he turns color; then cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize his stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	From the obstruction of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at any time for him not to pierce all the very fine spatium according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then open the very subtle gap of the bladder, and hold it closed for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, and then replace it; but perhaps it is not necessary, because the strong urine will not leave the gap closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the gap is small, it is a sign of a weak bladder, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the perforation in their place are blighted, for none are born with a perforation at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marrow, and it is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the head of the penis and the shaft are stretched as if it were a feather, so that the perforation can be made in the correct place; and be careful to prevent bleeding which often occurs, and if it does happen, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this foulness appears on the penis, and it is either malignant or benign; it is necessary that you prick them with a subtle needle, scrape them, and wash them thoroughly, then apply moist cotton in an Egyptian ointment, and continue the healing treatment with a fine ointment until it is cured.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the foulness is malignant, with putrid color and odor, it is necessary that you treat it with cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have it, and if the splint is in a sleep like a stick, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the splint that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you are certain about the condition of the stick, it will turn black and corrupt in its core and roots; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupt, then cover it with a paste made from apple bark and eggs, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is most effective in two ways: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the matter of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, it is necessary that you insert or guide a plug into the urethra and let the patient urinate; and when the hair at the head of the penis is dry, on those who have not been circumcised, or there is an abscess or fistula, in such cases, then you must scrape it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and free the matter from the penis on all sides; and if it is a difficult task to plan this, then scrape it gently at the top of the penis and the scrotum with a spatula; then separate them slightly and cover it immediately with a thin cloth dipped in cold water so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest work for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children because they do not practice it in their laws, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have observed the greatest part of masters and elders who practiced circumcision near the anus, with force, and at every new moon; it was because there are two layers, and perhaps one might cut off this one and preserve that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns with the cover, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleaning which is from the deep wound, the point of the member is not assured; and at the cleaning of the nail, by chance, the iron escapes, and it damages the work, and often they heal in such a way that they do not need cleaning and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with force on all the thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well from above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if the thread is cut evenly all around, but it should be well twisted around the skin; and the manner of the first operation must make the child think that you are not tying the thread too tightly around the stick, but then let it relax in every way possible. Then twist it between your fingers straight, and hide the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the infant does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then press your hand against the stick and blow into its heart, and pull it up until the end of the stick is clean; then clean it well from all the dirt gathered on it, and tie it with a double thread, and bind it to another thread; and hold it by the second tie in the pouchet (a small pouch) and at the tip index (likely a finger); and cut between the two threads, then lift the heart gently and pull the stick's chief; then let the blood flow bit by bit, for that is how it heals; and sprinkle it with powder, and cover it with a gluey cloth made of half-boiled egg mixed with rose water, good oil, and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with other remedies as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of cleansing is this: both shoulders should be held still and cut, and the arm should also be long and equal.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when the veins burst during incision; then you must extend your finger so that the vein does not become infected; cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tweezers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and the area under the wedge is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, and gently remove the skin; cut it as much as you can, and be careful to avoid the wedge part of the limb, which will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the burn of a sudden wound from fire, which we have spoken about in treating burns, and if one pulls with too much force, it will go worse, so do not harm; treat it, as we said, as long as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the blockage caused by a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a newborn, or similar conditions, as we have said in that division; and if the urine cannot be released, and you see the retention is due to a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be made to bend over on his knees; he should be placed on his back with pressure on his belly above his back, and the patient should be restrained as much as possible. This forces the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, allowing the urine to flow; if it does not come out, as we said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction to all instruments called "syringes," which have this shape: they should be made of fine, light silver, like a bird's feather, with a length of about 3.5 inches (8 cm).
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for urination is as follows: take a double thread and tie it to the top of a wool or cotton ball, then insert the thread into the urethra; cut off the excess wool and insert it all the way up to the top of the urethra, then lubricate the syringe with oil or butter and egg albumen, and have the patient sit down. Gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over the syringe; next, withdraw the syringe before the bladder is emptied, and have the patient feel for the point where the flow stops, and if it is not done in this order, because the direction in which the urine flows is twisted. Then cut the thread through all the wool bits, and the urine will follow the thread; remove it forcefully and let the patient urinate; repeat with the syringe until the bladder is completely emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or pus appear in the bladder, due to its putrefaction, you should view it and let water and medications distill, using the entire instrument called "clepsydre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; the chevelure (hair or texture) of the medicine must be such that it stops the flow well without addition, if it can draw out the moisture and push as needed; and when you see your medicines settling in the bladder, place the head of the vessel into the moisture and draw out the liquid gently. Draw out the liquid completely, then press firmly; if the moisture enters back in, it will go directly to the bladder, which the patient will feel; this is the form of a delicate enema by which one enemas the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the place is higher; then open the chest from the side where the ribcage splits; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you intend to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and warm the moisture over fire; then insert the tip of the enema bag into the anus, and squeeze your hand on the bladder until all the moisture enters the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and pierce it roundly; thread a strong string through these holes, then arrange the circle as one would arrange a dal, and put inside what you intend to use: oil, moisture, and water; tie it with the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture enters the bladder.
de la piere	from stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for dealing with stones and their extraction alongside medicinal practices; I have also explained the distinction between stones causing pain in the kidneys, and all the signs to look out for, and which type of stone requires surgical intervention; whether in the bladder or the urethra, and I will convey this to you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute urine retention due to its thin quality; it opens up the urinary tract, greatly distressing the patient, often with pain, and then it hardens; it attacks the foundations many times; the healing process is light for children under four years old, but very difficult for the elderly, and affects those in their middle age most moderately. The treatment is less severe for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a cleanse to draw out all foulness from the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often entangles itself with the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and upright them, moving them away from each other so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, never rising up again; then place the patient's hands between his legs, with his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then tie him down and feel inside. If you sense the stone in a particular space, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come away by touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and the patient will be relaxed, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and strong; then press it into its foundation, grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, at the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and the stone will come out from where you saw it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the cutting is done; then he should use the spoon-shaped instrument, which is as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the scrotum and the base, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and your two legs should be together at the base, and the urethra should be cut wide enough to prevent obstruction, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the stone at the base causes it to come out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: these are difficult to pass; and if they are below, resembling a spearhead or rounded, with an easy passage.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary to use pincers that are also like a file at the top to pull the stone so that it does not escape; or you can bend a fine curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot do it thus, enlarge the opening slightly and if the skin is torn, pull with vitriole; and if there is more than one stone, first pull the largest one into the neck of the bladder, then cut, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they must cut it out carefully, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For there are two things that can happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine returns immediately, as the muscles cannot be sewn together; but nevertheless, make every effort to pull it out, either with pincers or by removing pieces, until you have finished. When you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, tighten it, and place a moist cloth of oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, on the hot abscess to soothe it; then bind the patient tightly to his bed for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of hot and cold blood rises from the joint, then apply healing ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions appear in the wound and congelations of blood in the bladder, and urine retention occurs without any sudden discharge: then press your finger into the wound and extract the pus, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause illness; then clean the wound with water and oil and heat, and aid it in every way you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that for all these treatments, you tie both legs together and apply medicines to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, stuck, and urine cannot pass; then if you treat it as I say, cutting it many times, it is excusable for the cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the forefront according to this form, and fix it at three angles in the wood:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra beyond the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently twist the iron inside the urethra until it reaches the stone; and keep twisting the iron in the urethra little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken and jumps out with urine, and hurts the patient; and you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then take a needle and thread, and sew the stone from below and another from above, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the string, and clean the frozen blood in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones" (a reference to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare for women to have stones, and when they do, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not easy to find a woman well-versed in medicine who understands these matters, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is such that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of healing; and the fourth way is that the stone in a woman's side is often more pressing than in a man's, so it needs to be cut deeper, and much fear attends it. If need be, you must summon a mistress well-knowing in this art, and if she cannot be found, then do not seek her out; instead, present a wise woman skilled in women's lives, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you have commanded regarding the examination of the stone. And take great care that this woman is chaste: then she should press her right thumb into the base of the stone, and seek it out; if she finds it, she should hold it there under her left hand on the swollen bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; until it reaches the middle of the bone, where it is moved and feels the stone in that part; and do not move your hand above or below the stone, make the first cut small. Then turn the ratchet in the thigh, if you feel the stone deeply in the wound, as long as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and with thorns.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, take vitriole (a strong acid) and grind it into a powder, and hold it over the wound for an hour until the pain is alleviated; then return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard, and have tools that I have told you for removing stones from people to aid you in your task; and if the wound does not heal, and it is an artery that has been cut, sprinkle powder on the wound and apply bandages and splints, and do not repeat this, leaving the stone and never pulling it out unless the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat from the blood is calmed and the limbs are relaxed, return to your work as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	from herniated cartilage
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rameous aquose is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white matter, which is detached from the heart of the tissues that contain the blood, and it is called 'syfac', and never properly part of the tissue of the blood, if one thinks it is another tissue; and this is the thin layer of tissue between the white matter we have mentioned. And this does not occur naturally.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this rameous is due to weakness that affects the tissues, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from a percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: sometimes it is pale yellow, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and so forth; and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses are bright, very long like the figure of a serpent, and do not open the joints, because they are covered in moisture all over.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, then the abscesses are bright with a part of the serpent's head, and for this reason one thinks it is another serpent; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white as we have said, then it smells very good. Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the innermost parts, from which the shape will be known before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his ability and the condition of his body; then place him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and cover him with many sheets; then have him sit on his left side, and command the healer to sit at his right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs near the heart; then take the scalpel, and cut through the skin among the ribs from top to bottom towards the elbow, making a clean incision in considering the skin of the ribs until it is white, and carefully remove the flesh without damaging the rib; then make an opening in the flesh with water at a wide gap, and extract all the fluid, and then apply your bandages, and close the opening; and do not touch the heart of the rib, but only the flesh; cut around it carefully, that if you do not cut it well, the fluid may return. And if an error occurs in your work, bring it back to its original state when you have completed the work with the scalpel. Then sew together the two parts of the rib near the heart, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt about the flow of blood; then cut off the clot from all the suspension, and extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the arrow is divided into two parts, knowing that these are two branches, then cut off the other part as you have done with the first, and drain the blood, and apply to the wound a clean cloth moistened in rose oil; and put on another clean cloth moistened in wine and oil, and place the two coils above it, and cover them with doubled cloths, and bind it tightly according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use the linen cloth according to this form, and join them together with stitches at the crotch of the breeches, and one of them pin over the base up to the back, and the other part at the palm; and the third above the two angles, and tie all the restrictions in the loop of the breeches. Never use this cautery ramage with a hot iron, but rather use a delicate surgical knife, cut through the skin of the coions, and heat it as we have said, so that the white satisfying substance that contains the water is exposed; if you take the cautery according to this form, pierce that satisfying substance at the same time, and scrape off with this hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the surgeon in all ways that you can, as long as you draw out everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move with caution from blood clotting, and consider the tasks of cutting; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or a blood clot or any other thing, cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then perform an incision as I have told you, and be certain through the signs that we have mentioned that the dislocation is caused by moisture; so place the patient in a raised position. Then incise the abscess from below towards the whole area, making a wide opening, and insert the probe into the length of the body; let the pus flow out completely. Then apply cotton and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain, then treat the wound until it heals. If the white cloth does not allow the pus to drain from the wound's opening, then you should use a quill or an instrument used to draw off water from the dropsical patient, as has been mentioned before; widen the wound, and be aware that the pus will come back, and it will gather again after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, in this way the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	You know that in this branch there are many dire conditions, which is why I think it is better to leave it as it is; and I will tell you about the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come where there are hairs, especially in the skin; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know from the excessive sour and bitter fluid that extends to the hairs, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the skin; it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are numerous grayish, black, or foul-smelling abscesses, and they do not come from a new artery or vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, if it is blocked by the arrangement of hot inflammation in that part, when you press it with your fingers; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	What is made of vein inflammation is blocked by its arrangement due to the touch of the fingers, and it can be cut well on this model and on other parts; and it is that you take the heart of the veins, then there is warmth at the top, and the white part becomes stronger, and liberates the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already hard with these cuts, then you must extract the vein and cut it; and if it is white, or in what is inside the vessels, then you must release all that tension and cut it properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the base of the hair is behind, it is necessary that you cut it all off, and extract the root, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, immediately apply a moist woolen compress with rose oil and wine to the wound, and then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the hairs
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed in a similar wrapping like a boil, with the hair becoming thick and entangled, and it causes the patient great pain when it appears; and its treatment is just as careful, if not more so, than the one mentioned above, and we will tell you about the work of it, according to what the ancients have done.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should place the patient in a comfortable, elevated position, then squeeze the suspended veins below your fingers to their full extent, encompassing all vessels close to the limb, and stretch them taut; then, using a sharp spatula, cut across the exposed vessels, as we have said for extracting arteries in temples, then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and bind it to the first joint where the vein entered, and likewise to the other end; then, cut them evenly, according to the length of the body, and remove any corrupted moisture. Treat the wound like others, so that no vessel leaks, for by doing so, all veins will receive their nourishment, and the organs will not dry out or be unable to aid themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The outcome of this branch is from the rupture that occurs either at the site of the sinew (syfac) or in the extension on the belly in the region of the angles, causing the intestines to descend from this rupture to one of the coils; and this rupture can be either due to the syfac or the extension, and these two methods have similar causes: percussion, a jump, straining, lifting a heavy weight, and similar actions; and the signs when it is due to the extension of the syfac are that it happens little by little over a long period, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess remains evenly sized towards its complete formation, as the syfac pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the incision that sudden pain arises, and various abscesses appear beneath the skin close to it, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and blood from the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the abscess with the intestine, it remains stuck, causing great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with pain, for this reason one must be careful.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the procedure is that you command the patient to straighten the intestine in his hand within the wound if it can be done; then carefully hold it between your hands and loosen the joints; then extend the heart above, and cut all the skin from the length; then insert the fingers inside the folds of the skin, following the need to open the wound, so that they can come out; then peel off the healthy tissue that is underneath the skin, as long as the white tissue is hard and fully exposed on all sides; then with your index finger, follow the course of the fold of the skin, between the white tissue below the outer skin and the second tissue, and behind the first one, and in front of it; and afterward, with your right hand, inside the heart of the fold of the skin, place the white tissue above in your left hand, and loosen the organ towards the tailbone; and command the assistant to stretch the organ upward, and untie what is attached at the rear behind the ligament; and check both hands if there is no intestine wrapped up or hard white tissue, and if you find anything, insert it into the abdomen underneath; then take a needle with a thick thread made of X threads, and pass it through the posterior part of the white tissue, after the skin of the fold; then cut the parts that appear to have threads, as long as there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the white tissue we mentioned, which is underneath the outer skin, with a strong thread from two sides; then wrap the parts around the threads, and tie them in such a way that none of their strands can enter inside, preventing an abscess; and put the binding according to the first long binding, two fingers' length away from it, and after these two bindings, leave the white tissue underneath the heart of the fold of the skin as one finger's length; and afterward, follow the contour of the organ with the remainder of the white tissue, as we previously mentioned; then moisten wool in oil and apply it to the wound, and bind it with the thread we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white part as we have said, after incision, out of fear of further bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leaves the wound open as long as it needs to heal; if it takes time to close, then apply hot water, and do as we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	from meat hernias
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this condition, never have I seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the elders say that it is made like a root that holds a joint together, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting them lightly on the inside, and then open the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels close; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur suddenly, as we have said, and open the vessels; nor should any part of the intestines protrude, and if it does, it is a sign of danger, and all efforts must be made to repair it; however, if it persists too long at this point, one believes it to be a wound or an abscess, until the intestines protrude; and this occurs due to the expansion of the syphac, which is attached to the vessel, as we have said before, because it becomes expanded then softened and swollen, opening the vessels; and its cure is by cauterization, as we have previously stated; and never should it be cured in this manner with iron. And let the patient lie on his back, then make an incision along the ruptured area, according to the quantity of three fingers' width; and then extract the syphac that is under the skin, take a stick and place it on top of the visible part of the syphac; press firmly in the abdomen, cut both visible parts of the syphac at the base of the stick, and remove them; then remove the stick, do not cover or extend the wound, nor anything else, as I have told you about the cure for the rupture of intestines; and treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become contaminated and the wound heals, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the fracture, but the cauterization is moved in this place, and it is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the hard skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the joints becomes softened in no particular place because the muscles inside are relaxed, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wishes to treat it, to lay the patient on his back and cut off the soft skin that has become separated from the natural skin; then bring the two edges together with a stitch, and if there is too much soft skin, cut it away at three stitches or four firmly; then cure it like other wounds as long as it heals, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	This medical treatise offers remedies and procedures for various ailments and injuries
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that cauterization is prohibited by our laws, and for that reason, I would not speak of it in this book; however, it is necessary to mention it in two ways: one is to respond wisely when asked about it, and to provide the appropriate cure; and the other is because we often need cauterization on certain animals to help us, as with goats, sheep, cats, and other creatures.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that cauterization is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we perform by attraction, make the animal sit in hot water until the joints become soft and supple; then press them with your hand while they are restored and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	On castration of the penis: it is necessary to tie up the animal and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle one by one until they are well scraped; and leave no drop of blood, nor any subtle discharge that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is superior to that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, something from the joints may remain, leading the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound as long as it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two manners like men: one is when between the two sexes the appearance opens up also as the figure of a woman, with hair and never cuts himself short.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, who have a penis on their hand as a phallus and two vulvas.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you apply the appropriate compresses to all the affected parts, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the hair
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tendons are a tight structure attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and no woman has ever had such a strong hand, and it is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should remove the excess of tendons in your hand or fingers, and cut them gently; do not cut too deeply, so that bleeding does not occur, and treat it with another cure until it is healed; and for another condition that appears at the opening of the wound, and its use, and perhaps jumps out, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to deal with it, as we have said of the splinter, and treat it while it is clean.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of a woman is not properly understood, or if the opening is small; it is innate by birth, or accidental due to illness that comes upon her, or perhaps because of an unnatural fit, or a subtle or specific affliction, and it can affect her in any part—in the middle, on one side, underneath, or wherever; and it requires knowledge of conception, childbirth, and sometimes even the flowers (meaning possibly breast milk) to be considered. The understanding of these things is through observation of the body's movements.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the dislocation is recently apparent, whether it occurs in the hand or the foot.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If the dislocation is subtle and recent, act swiftly: place your two index fingers together, and have the patient lie on their back with their legs spread; then form both shoulders into arcs until the subtle dislocation is reduced and the joint is stable; then take wool, soak it in oil, and apply it to the joint, keeping the patient on their back each day so they cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the dislocation is hard and persistent, it is necessary that you use a spatula-like instrument resembling a fir branch.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from fire, suspend it at the oncine (a term for a specific point or area) and apply a poultice; have medicines that stop blood flow, such as mithridate, dragon's blood, incense, and a sufficient amount of egg; then administer a large piece of plont (a fabric or material used in bandaging) so the wound cannot close; and do this for a long time, and then apply a dry linen tent; and thus continue with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the swelling comes from moisture, it should be covered according to this manner; if it is not an abscessed swelling.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Because an abscess that is enlarged in the wound of the mare should not be touched with fire.
