des emorroides	from hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without usual care, become inflamed; and as they age, they turn into these; and in the previous section, we discussed the appearances, symptoms, and signs, and I will now discuss those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their inflammations, when they are at their worst in the mare (anus), and do not appear to be felt, can only be cured properly with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the wound, one can feel, are those that one can heal.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore advisable that you place the woman in a cold house, then gently apply plasters to her breasts and roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders to stop the flow of blood, such as ginger and dragon's blood and incense, and similar substances; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, and immerse her in cold water. And if bleeding persists, let it be treated with a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and gall nuts and similar things, and then take flour from barley, mix it with honey and butter, and make an ointment to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes wet, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If that does not work, apply cupping glasses to the back and around the mammary area without causing injury; then take lint and dampen it in plantain or mulberry juice mixed with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has rested, continue the treatment with clean bandages as long as it remains healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so it should be covered as I have said before; then cure it as long as it remains healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	from the abscess of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the breast, such as a chancre, previous abscess, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, along with many other illnesses mentioned in the prior discussion.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatment about the hot abscess that occurs in the breast, which is not like other abscesses that discharge pus; and if you are knowledgeable about the work of fire, consider whether the abscesses are red in their onset, full of heat and fever, and turn red as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make the patient suffer until the pain is eased; then have the ill-person sit, and take two small seats where he can recline, and rest on his back, spreading his legs in a way that lengthens the affected part of the leg. Then spread his thighs, put his arms beneath his knees, and tie them firmly with a good band; then open the anus towards the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, from which this form comes. And it is important that when you insert this instrument, you first push the right end inside to see the depth of the wound, so that whatever enters the wound with the instrument does not go any deeper than it should, and it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the deep part of the wound with cloth so that the instrument does not cause discomfort.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and they make an incision with a soft hand, if it is necessary to cover the wound, then use a spatula; and when the bowel is empty, it is necessary to put moist cloth in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound up to the margin of the wound, and place a clean wet cloth over the wound on top of the abscess and the forearm, and then wrap it with a cloth soaked in water and cooked malva; then cure after two days of treatment until it is healed; and never lift the abscess or the wound by enema with water and honey, and then with water or cooked roots of lis and aristologe; and then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the abscess, it is necessary to be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Skill is first in the dance, knowing the figure of natural childbirth, and its signs are when you see the woman straining down and desiring to smell the air: then hasten for the child to be born; then know that these children are according to their proper form, and come second with them; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child comes quickly; for as it descends upon its head, it second them with him, and the mother's body rids itself of its excesses through good purification; and this one who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never stops coming upon their feet, and affects the body or the joint, or the hands, or comes upon their belly, or back, and turns by chance onto their neck, and other evil positions; so it is necessary for a skilled helper to be wise and subtle in these matters, and to ward off error and disappointment, and I will show you all the positions as to how he should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the evil comes upon his head from natural causes, and a woman gives birth heavily, and her virtue is weak, then she should sit on a saddle, or women should hold her; and take the nature of oil or fennel that has been cooked, and then apply the baile (probably a type of herbal compress or poultice) between her fingers in the shape of a small spatula.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut through the second joint, and saw it from its finger as much as the moisture that is stuck inside; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fennel seeds in musk with oil of sesame; then make her sneeze and blow her nose, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, it is necessary that you gently reset them little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up high; then take the seat off the ground, turn the woman so she does not stand up, and if her hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut through the hand at the joint closest to the body, extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the exit of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on his feet, he needs to be pushed up, and then he moves back and forth little by little until they are even; then press on the feet and extend them a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He can jump up to his ankles if he is commanded to press, and this makes him sneeze from the condition; if he jumps further, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, he moves back and forth little by little according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not work as we have said, take some musk, and oil of clary, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; apply this remedy to the woman's womb both inside and out, then let her lie in warm water reaching down to her ribs; when she is moistened, make a collar of mirra and place it around her, leaving it for an hour. Then have her sit, then make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose, and gently massage her stomach, for the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the emergence of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, he moves his hands little by little; then he turns over on his collarbone, and his feet hang down, and he lies on his side; he bends his hands little by little, then takes hold of his hands on his belly, and removes the cushions from below, until he is completely relaxed downwards; if the child does not cry, take his feet and move them, then move his belly upwards, then turn your hands inside out; and bring the child little by little; and tell the woman to press herself as the child comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie on her side with her legs bent; then administer the musk or salve I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, and study how to bring back the hand; deliver the child according to its natural position, and have her sneeze, and command that she press as the baby is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its mother's chest, with its hands spread and its face turned away from its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold their hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is even, apply a light, muscular and oiley compress, as we have said, then command that it moves slightly by slight movement; and once you have done this, leave it in that position, and tell them to breathe deeply; and make them sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it acts in this way for all the rest, if the seconding (unclear term) is on your finger, drain the moisture; and if it sticks to its face and neck, cut it from the corner of the mouth so it is not held back, and the child will die; then pull the baby out, as you have placed it properly, and command the woman to breathe deeply. Then gently release.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the emergence of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at once; and this is not a strange thing, as it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are a strange thing and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their destinies are determined by the one who divides them, who is connected to the mother's womb; and they never emerge as naturally as any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they scream loudly, if the treatment is as we have said, and there are skilled healers, then make it happen quickly and gently; and do so as it deserves to be done for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in stages I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they take the form of a child according to the noble measure, and it is necessary that the skilled healer knows all this, for sometimes a similar thing happens; so do as is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	From the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child in the womb, as I mentioned in the previous section, and there is no discharge, and you are forced to perform manual labor; it is important that you know if the woman is of healthy constitution and does not have any fear or concern about the death; she should be placed on her back, with her legs inclined downwards and raised, and the midwife should attend to her for as long as she is in bed, without allowing her to move down to deliver the child. Then, wet your fingers with moist olive oil mixed with althae and fennel powder and flaxseed, and apply this mixture to the woman's perineum with gentle rubbing. After that, gently press on the area where the stitches are, then carefully insert the finger in the orifices that are suitable for delivery, and ensure the child is descending onto her head. If the descent is on her feet, sides, or under the chin, carefully insert the fingers in these positions as well, and if the delivery is easy, gently press the fingers against the stitches, between the two middle fingers of your left hand, while holding the corbeille (a birthing tool) with your right hand, and deliver it all with a slight movement. Insert the finger into any of the mentioned positions until the matter becomes clear. This is the shape of the stitch:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then hold it equally in movement from one side to the other, to pull it out, and be the dislocation sharp so that it holds firm, as this shape demonstrates.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a piece remains, and none of its edges are oiled, press it into that part and draw the other part; if nothing remains, move this dislocation higher up the limb and do so until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward over the other and cannot return due to tightness, it is necessary that you wrap it with a cloth until it comes out entirely; then cut at the joint of the finger or the thumb, and do the same for the other hand, and have both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's foot is large and twisted at birth, and has a sharp edge, it is necessary that you insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and press and extract the edge; or you can use the instrument called 'almidach', with which the form is made with the tools of this chapter; and in the same way, make the foot move naturally; then carefully pull the bones with pincers, and if the foot jumps out and is constrained by force, it may be split; as long as the moisture at the worst exit is removed; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the wound is slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the belly or the bowels, it is necessary to pull it with the drape wrapped around the hand; and make an incision on the belly or the bowels as much as the moisture that is inside; and if the other members are broken and the feces remain, he should press his hand from the wound towards the mouth of the wound, and pull it forcefully; then he should incise or cut, and remove it; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to the heat of the abscess that has formed, it is not necessary to work on it, but rather to apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, and soak with soft water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocation is on his side and you can set it straight, you must do so as we have said for a live child; and if that cannot be done, cut it off in pieces, leaving nothing of the fragment.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for abscesses that come from veins; and if bleeding occurs, use sharp restraints, and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been cut open and a child removed; then another was cut open above it, and the other child was saved.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there comes one abscess in the cheek, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I couldn't heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because that belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, until the woman was in a better condition; and after a long time, she still had a little bowing of her arm; and I have never remembered this chapter being written for any other reason than that, when the masters encounter something strange, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the wife back to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the press, with which books are bound; and at its turn, to the two corners of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth should have a diameter of two fists, with margins of one palm and a half; and between the two halves, there should be an adjustment of this same horn, firm on both sides, measuring half a palm or a little more; and this adjustment is inserted into the opening of the mare's mouth to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; it should have two adjustments, each one palm-length wide with a width of two fingers; when opening the mare's mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman lie down on her side, with her legs spread apart. Then, press the two adjustments together inside the mare's mouth and hold the handle of the instrument between her thighs; subsequently, open your hand over the instrument as you did with the pliers, according to how far you need to open the mare's mouth, until it reaches its desired position.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all diverse, and their appearances are many; and when you have arranged them in order, the work is done more swiftly, and they prove more useful for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument even if you have not arranged it, for the need for it is not an excuse for carelessness.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage of labor is reached, if it is necessary to hold back the patient from pushing, you must instruct her to retain her breath and then force her to exhale forcefully; grasp her hands and press them against her mouth and nose, and if she stops breathing through this, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not done, I will take a needle or a plug, and make a perforation or an opening, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, dill, fennel, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or steeped in water over the fire; then place one end of a plug or needle into the opening, and the other end in the mouth of the wound, and hold it until the vapors enter the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient's condition worsens,
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment it remains immobile, and is not strong, instruct the patient to moisten his left hand with oil of sesame or musk, then return it to its natural position, and want the second one; and when she finds it, press and stretch it little by little straighteningly, so that the pain does not occur during extraction; but you must move it slightly to the right and to the left, and then treat it.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the wound is very tight, we have mentioned the cure of sneezing and herb fumigation; and if it does not improve from all that we have said, be careful not to drain it; but it is necessary that whoever has an opening in the wound, you tie it to the woman's ankle, then apply a four-part ointment; she will sneeze and expel it, and come out strong; however, if she sneezes, a bad odor comes from the stomach and head, and the patient becomes worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then suitable fumigations should be used: no one among the ancients has tried fumigation with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman to retain the flowers and the seed is this one:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a bell, and the narrow part is inserted into nature, and the wider part is placed over the fire; and the fumigation should be on coals, and the steam until it is spent, and then another is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the base
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their base pierced, but it is covered by a subtle mark: therefore, one must teach the midwife to pierce that mark with a fine tool, and do not use an aggressive instrument, and protect the wound so that she does not touch it; then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, and apply the dressing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, pierce a string of silk or gut, and leave it for several days, and it will fall out when the child wants to move around in bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this stoppage of a wound or abscess suddenly; it is necessary to cover this stoppage: if it is healed, as we have said about the pain of bleeding.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula deep within the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that originate from below the foundation are called nodations, and those that come from outside the foundation defying gravity, or in the space between two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it opens, and still emits white or subtle smoke, and these fistules do not heal; they are known because of the discharge or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they jump out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they perforate the fistulas that reach the bladder, and half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and the root of the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus you recognize the persistent fistula in the fundament, and it is not passing: and it is that you insert your index finger into the fundament, and press an extremely thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula where there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you insert a thin point, or a horsehair, as long as you feel the point or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with discharge or wind, as we have said: know that it will not pierce; be haste in curing.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to a urethral channel, if it bleeds while urinating and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is cut just above the joint of the thigh, then the veins nearby become inflamed; if there is no curvature or unusual sensation of pain around it, and it continues to persist, then it is not cured by any medicine or treatment; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure other than hard work and the vain attempts of foolish people who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor old and there is hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced, the patient lies on their back with their legs raised to their armpits, and their thighs inclined towards their stomach; then apply a tent-like bandage, or a tight wrap if there is curvature, until you know where the vein is located.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep inside, it is necessary to press your index finger there, and he will feel that the pain is coming from a specific point; if you uncover or feel between your thumb and forefinger the satisfaction or hardness, then know that it is persistent; unless it works itself out, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can in any case do nothing well enough, but this happens rarely; and the aid one provides consists of applying a gentle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as mentioned above; heating it thoroughly inside the fistula until it reaches the foundation, and repeating this process two or three times, until you know that these hardened spots are burned, which resemble a feather from an eye; then apply moist bandages, until the swelling subsides, and finally dress with something that soothes, binding it tightly.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he cannot be healed in any other way; and if a thread enters between the fingers, and does not pierce through to the flesh which is at the base of the finger, and there is a thick covering of skin or tissue, and you see a fistula following this covering towards the heart, then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and pull out again before the thread, and then apply cautery afterwards, as long as it comes to the edge of the thread; and the thread will be delivered and cut. Then beware of those false threads that look like a bird's feather, and do not touch them in any way.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain persists, and the fire or medical treatment does not help, then cauterize it with either fire or a sharp tool.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery combines two good things: that is to say, the burning of these prepared parts, and the drawing out of blood and the drying of moisture; then apply moist ointment or crushed material from a plant while the bones are bent, and push the burned parts into the socket; then treat the wound with hot coals from a hard wood, and these dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not relapse.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears right through to the bottom of the fundament, and it is distant from the body, if you press your finger into its origin, and feel it, then this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tentation, and between them is the web or the sticky or charred, and it is about to pierce, if there is no other way of escape and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to the bottom, or if you can insert something and cure it as before; but don't go too deep, that you do not remove the covering which holds the foundation, and complications arise from the contrary; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or you remove that cover and clean it afterward, when it has been cut away from the base, either with a knife or another instrument pointed; then cleanse the infected wound, as much as you can; study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And they never form fistulas in this manner: and it is when you press the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side near the foundation of the skin above, if a small tent-shaped piece is taken at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And they insert the thread twisted in two, and press the tent along the entire thread into the fistula as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is deeply embedded at the edge of the foundation within, then pull the thread out of that opening, thus pressing your other finger or foundation into it; and hold the top of the thread, bringing the two parts together, and fasten them to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and do not touch it again until the threads break apart, and the wound is healed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, try to pierce it in every way you can, but if it is too tightly closed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if it is not done carefully due to the tightness of the closure, and then treated as we have said, while it is still healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form is a sharp, spiky point that is used to make the fistula; it is thick and pierced both ways; on one side too hard, and on the other too soft, so that it is neither cut nor should be cut, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids exist in two ways: either they are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, with small or large protrusions, and cause bleeding; or they extend from the anus and are located at the base, sometimes alone or in groups, and have a purplish color. For the treatment of hemorrhoids that are internal, instruct the patient to stay in bed until the anus heals completely and the pain subsides. If they cannot be held in place by their own moisture, use cloth, cotton, or a piece of camel's hair to tie them; cut them off at the base, then powder them with hot powders suitable for cauterization; or apply the cautery as described in the chapter on cautery, treating other conditions as needed until they heal. If the anus cannot be opened, administer a harsh enema to wash out what is inside so it can be expelled easily. The treatment is easier when the patient's pain and the protrusion of the hemorrhoids have subsided, and the incision should be made with caution using a blade.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary, you must administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wrap it around an needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread beneath the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all the others, leaving one for draining the excess blood; then place a moist cloth on the wound, either in rose oil or wax, and cover it, and instruct the patient to rest. And then leave it until the stitches heal, and when they have fallen off, apply treatment and other remedies until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully and precisely from the roots or foundations
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is a drying up of roots in the intestine, due to restrictive nature or when the disease is old and no medicine helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the skin with the point of a spatula or your finger, ensuring it does not retain moisture. Then treat it as it should be until it heals; if it cannot heal, repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it feels moist and is cut; then treat it until it is cured.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The mouse is a small, hairy creature that moves stealthily before the body, and it goes in many places; it never causes pain, and one feels as if they were dead from trembling, affecting the whole body especially the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from a goose's wing or a strong eagle's feather, and place that feather on the trembling until it turns the whole trembling red; then turn your hand over the entire feather until you cover all around the trembling, and set it straight, and remove the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle and draw them from below and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut, so as to keep both, and press gently. And if you see, cauterize the wound, just as it is in front of or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never should one use a enema of silver or bronze, or melted iron or wire; and never should these small and large instruments be used according to those to whom they are entrusted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are thus poorly cared for in the treatment of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bladder is small and wide at the top, or the abdomen is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is a distension, or the abdomen is bound in this way, and the feces are within, as you see, then have one side of the abdomen pierced, and the other sealed; and place into the abdomen medicinal herbs from an animal bladder or parchment, piercing it all around with small holes, leaving one space between each hole, and insert a strong thread twisted in an X shape or similarly around each hole, and gather up the abdomen like a bowstring; then apply the enema instrument to the mouth of the thread, and perform the enema; this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm compress with oil or goose fat or something similar to the head, then gently squeeze it; then the minister should grip it with both hands together until it is completely drained, then remove the compress and help the patient raise their legs against the wall, and let the medicine drain out as much as possible; if they sleep for a whole night, it is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a stomach disorder and the medicine drains quickly, then it should recur as long as it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the foundation or in an abscess, it should be treated with equally delicate enemas as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate enema which tightens the skin.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are by the impact of stone, and sword and knife cuts, or spear, arrow, or axe, or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or side, or belly, or liver, and similar parts; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, beginning with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head or neck, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by a stone or similar objects, and the skin is nevertheless deeply cut and the wound is large, and you doubt an abscess: treat it promptly, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and dress it in the opposite way from the affected part; and give the patient wine and lean meats to reduce swelling.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healed, let his flesh be reduced, and he should not drink wine or eat char; and apply a poultice of rose oil only, or aromatic wine; and if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood, and do not move it with air or powder, which I will speak of shortly; and if the fire has moved it, apply some ointment, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together like tent flaps, then bring them together with stitches, as I will say about abdominal wounds, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed through the bone, and it bleeds profusely, but only for a short while, then apply pressure; afterwards treat the wound with medicine and replace the skin with hard flesh instead of leather, and instruct the patient to eat substantial meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in a wound that does not reach the bone, and it bleeds continuously, then drain it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which no blood can stop, even with medicine, then cut the artery, and if you cannot do so, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize the wound.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: it is that you put this powder which hardens so that the fire can move it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method for the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts of fresh charcoal, mix the powder finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it so that it spreads well and joins together with all its moisture; then bind it tightly and leave it unbroken unless it swells, for the medicine should not be removed as long as it remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used only, unless one has incense and dragon's blood, but the fire should move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no powder placed on it; but put some cooked herbs or a paste of barley flour made with water and honey, until it flows; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine pincers; and I will tell you below about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, with no distinction between this and that of the head, but if there is damage to the nerves or arteries in the neck.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy but to let them heal and put nothing restrictive on them, as that would harm the nerves and cause them to retract; do not apply any sharp objects to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member. But apply medicine under these conditions: just as chalk is washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cloth is also washed in sweet water and other herbs are added according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting through the muscles and tendons, treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected, filled with pus, pierce them to the bottom; if the artery is cut, and pus flows, if you mislead it, and the law, and cauterize improperly, and if there is a thorn in the throat or the heart, and the flow of blood must be stopped, do not touch the throat but remove it according to its natural shape; then apply the strictest bandage and leave it for no days, applying remedies until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, if you wish, and there are pieces of bone that cannot be removed, let them stay until the wound festered and becomes disfigured and lightens its discharge; and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, then consider the position of the wound in relation to the patient's vital parts: if the wound is mortal, do not apply powder in the first hour, nor bind it tightly so as to prevent the blood from clotting, for it may return to the body and cause further harm to the patient; but apply a soothing dressing twice a day. If you have no dressing, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and keep the patient sleeping on the wound for three or four days (or more); if there is no spasm, nor any unusual tremor or weakness in the body, then know that the wound is healing.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, and opens up, know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep, in front or behind, treat it accordingly; if large, sew it up; if small, use powder; and if it penetrates into the bone with pieces of shattered bones, dig out the debris if they are clean; if not, let the wound fester, and make the extraction easier; for other wounds in other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound, none of the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less than a small wound than a large one, because one must be more careful not to pinch the intestines, unless they are placed on top of each other; for the intestines tend to swell quickly and cause pain if they are pinched again, which is why the smaller wound is easier to manage, as we have mentioned before. You should know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of other wounds on the body and other specific sutures are common to other wounds; nevertheless, they are more appropriate for the suture of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing internal is affected, and it is a difficult thing to reset, it is by one of two methods: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water only slightly, or cook in water with salt, ginger, and pepper, and remove the intestines as soon as the swelling is gone; and never use wines that cause constriction, but let it be moved until it is deflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with either water or other bad fluids, then gently press it, for this lightens the entrance of a few things; and if it cannot enter, make a slight cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move the stool, that we should not cut it without great need; and this is the instrument to divide: it cuts inside the pile and pushes it out, observe this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine bursts out, put it back gently into its natural position if you have the ability, for it is better to move it.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and heels higher than the lower parts, and also be sure that the torn part of the belly is in one of the two parts, so that you attend to what I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have, then take in your hands a gentle medicinal oil that covers the entire tear, and gather the edges together; this is the common method of stitching. Press a needle or more through, according to the size of the wound, leaving two spaces at the top of the wound, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; pierce the two layers of skin with the two points of the scalpel, which are beneath the skin, until you have pierced that part, and gather together the two points of the scalpel all four together.
