Then tie the thread around the needle twice, then gather together the edges of the wound neatly, and insert another needle; tie it as you did with the first needle, and continue this work with needles according to your need until all the wound is secured. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, for the thin ones can pierce through all the flesh, and the very thick ones cannot go in well. Therefore, they should be medium. Do not push the needles too far outside the flesh and skin, or they will open up the wound before it is sewn; then trim off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping, and place tenting or a cloth at the ends of the needles to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is healed. This stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for there only needs one needle or two for stitching; this is how you sew up an injury that was caused by a knife on a man's belly, which was torn open, more than a palm-width wide, and it was away from the intestines by two palms, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought the intestine back after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, which was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any remedies, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither any medicine; and I applied clean cotton to the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thread it from the outer part to the inner part, right through the center; when it has pierced through completely, take hold of the thread with your thumb or stitch it where you first inserted the needle, and pierce it again from the inner part to the outer, until the stitching is complete. This method is such that you sew just as a tanner sews fur, leaving the thread once on one side and taking it up on the other, until the stitching is finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Gallens calls the proper way, is like no other, joining the two parts together naturally, and applying one end to the other with great skill: take a needle or thread close to the edge, pierce through only the outer layer, leaving the joints of the fabric untouched; then turn the needle and pierce from the opposite side towards the center, through both joints; and do the same on the other side, piercing through two other joints on either side. This is the most effective and common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen speaks these words, and many bear witness to the fact that when one has to sew up a stomach with two needles, each needle should have thread, and one needle should be inserted from one side, the other from the opposite side, just as those who sew up wounds do; and know this: when the opening is inside the stomach, the stitching will be more difficult than for other stomach wounds.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you pierce the fresh wound to all its blood, and the flesh has moved, then reapply the poultice with heating char, and if the flesh has moved, apply any present dressing, as long as the wound swells; and bind the thread, and make the bandage tight, and apply mirra; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, apply this immediately when it begins to swell, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these remedies for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is spreading to the principal members, it is necessary that you apply a light linen cloth soaked in hot temper oil, or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in swelling, and this happens often, then give it enemas of black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines. Then pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The inner organ called "young" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the weakness of the veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the edge of the wound falls off, like the intestine, it should be pushed back as well; while it is fresh, so that the blood does not clot, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away the tissue in between, and hang the two edges outside the wound from the opposite side until the extraction of the edge becomes easier.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it cannot be cured in any man, as I have seen a nobleman wounded in his belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of his stomach, it became inflamed and fistulated, and there issued evacuation and flatulence; I applied remedies according to my ability, and did not cease to try subtle treatments until he was healed and the wound made whole.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would not have trouble in his stomach; but he felt no pain, and improved in condition, eating and drinking as before. And none of the experienced healers said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in that manner: take a large reed, then gather together the edges of the wound, and when the reed has opened its mouth, place it between the two lips, so that it holds its mouth closed; then cut off the head of the reed, and this will hold it fast, and then place another reed in the same way until the wound is completely healed; and dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief is sharp inside the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be bound with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the chief of this intestinal thread, which is very clean, and bind it to the chief of the fine linen thread twisted, then thread it into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and arrange it in the wound; and this method of sewing is only valid according to reason and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestines, no one can heal it with such subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, whether it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it has hair and is deeply closed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the true nature hard and white, without feeling pain, and is also hairy like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it is slightly open, and at other times thick; sometimes soft, and at other times firm; and I have spoken about this in the discussion of wounds; that every wound which is not healed, and there is no discharge, comes from one of the nine causes: namely, through the purity or hardness of blood or pus; because of its evil nature; or because there is hard matter inside, preventing it from healing; or because there is too much pus; or because the muscles are spoiled, and the material is of poor quality; or because the medicine used for treatment is not good; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the properties in the region delay digestion, and delay health, and cause weakness by nature; or it has veins or bones, and I have already discussed all these causes, signs, and treatments with medicines in that section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I teach you the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body, for there are fistulas that involve large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the intestines, bladder, or any rib, or the spine at the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it affects a part belonging to the main member, and has similar characteristics.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is no cure but labor and ignorance; and if there is a fistula that does not come up to the place I mentioned, and you have hope for its cure, and understand it, take a piece of steel or iron, if the fistula is straight; and if it is crooked, seek a subtle plug to fit it, for the pus will bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has an opening in the hand through which it cannot be properly probed with plugs, wash it with one of the openings, for the moisture flows from one opening to another and cleanses it; then treat it as best you can, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is completely healed, and ask the patient in pain where he feels it most when you press your hand on it, and the place where he feels it. And when you truly know the place, and whether it is distant from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the places I told you, then cut it according to what I said, and remove all the foreign matter and corrupt flesh inside; and then cure it as best as you can, cutting it completely through as much as possible, then apply moistened medicine plasters, pressing them against the fistula until the medicine dissolves the excess that has accumulated at the bottom; and then put clean bandages over it, as long as it is healing; and if it does not heal in this way, cauterize it as we said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect your principal members, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed, with corrosion and blackening, then treat the matter urgently until the corruption is completely removed, then apply curative means until it is healed; and if it remains unhealed and bent as before, know that you are not yet able to proceed: expose and clean as much as you can, removing all the corruption, then restore it; and if thus it becomes healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep for you to treat; if there is no other cause but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can extract with tweezers using a suitable instrument, remove all of them, except none. And if moisture makes things worse, and there is no error or fear, cauterize and dry it up, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, apply something corrupting to the wound and let it rot until the bones are softened; then clean the wound. And if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, scrape off the corruption only until the blackness is completely gone, then treat the wound again; and if there is a great deal of corrupted tissue, extending almost to the bone; it should be carefully cut out and covered up until the wound heals. And I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can learn from his example and use this aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around 30 years old who had a pain in his leg due to something that arose inside the body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg and an abscess to form; he had no relief from it. But through their foolishness, they worked so much on the abscess that they corrupted many substances within, and it became a fistula, leading to numerous openings that leaked bowels and moisture from the body. For two years, many tried to cure him, but there was no skilled hand in the art of medicine; then I was called upon, and I examined his leg and the medicines used, as well as what was causing the abscesses to affect such large parts of his body. The young man's skin became red, with a citrine-like hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and found that some came into contact with each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then quickly seized one of the gaps and cut as deeply as I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and broken, and the corruption extended inward up to the bone; I understood what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had left; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but they could not unite it. Then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, and found that the corruption continued in the bone, so I treated it and then set it, and I focused on uniting it; but I was unable to do so until I had cut around one palm of the bone, and brought it back together with all its strength. Then I treated it again with medicines, and it healed and united quickly, without wanting to start over with the procedure again, except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the case of complete blood evacuation, but it was entirely healed, and a hard scar formed in place of the bone, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect from then on, neither to going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it is necessary to proceed in this manner: take a tie, and stretch it over the opening of the bone, and command anyone not to extend it upwards; and bind another thicker woolen tie over the first one, and fasten it to the flesh that is detached from the bone, pulling it so that you remove the corrupt flesh from underneath, and expose the flesh on the bone where you see fit; place coal or a table under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and be as careful as possible, as you can see and feel the corruption, and do this again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose the whole flesh; then place hot coals from one side to the other of the corruption, and be careful to close it up for a long time after the corruption has been cut out; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and close up the bone or the other part that contains it; and if the corruption is along two joints, there is no other tool but to cut them both off; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, this matter is very difficult, but you must nevertheless inquire about this corrosion how it opens, and cleanse it in every way that you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that there are many tools for cutting and closing these bones, according to their position and appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to adapt each tool to the work of each defect; and know that the operation will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the illnesses; choose therefore the tool that suits you best.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint becomes dislocated either internally or externally; and when you have treated the corruption with remedies, but they do not help, it is necessary to cover that member up to where the corruption originates, so that the patient may be saved from death or evil, which is greater, due to the fault of the member; and the sign of this is that the limb turns black, appearing as if it were burned by fire, and then turns purple after the corruption spreads from limb to limb throughout the body. If you hurry to cover it, especially if it's caused by the bite of some poisonous creature, like a sea scorpion or snake, and if the corruption is at the head of the affected area, treat it immediately and do not give it time to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, it should cut off at the joint, so that corrosion doesn't reach the arm; and if it comes up to the arm, it should cut through the shoulder; and if it passes through the shoulder, it's death, and no remedy is effective outside of its quantity of virtue; and thus it does with every corrosion on a bone: if it comes at the first joint, it cuts off after the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, it cuts through the entire foot; and if it rises in the leg, it cuts at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other device to save the patient from death; and the manner of cutting or binding the member is that you tie it tightly above and below, and extend one minister from each ligament downwards and upwards, and separate the flesh between the two ligaments with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed, then cut through or bind it, and place a strip of linen on each side, so that the linen doesn't touch the healthy part, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flow occurs when you operate, and you cauterize the wound too harshly or apply any restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the affected member with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to this man in great detail: he had a blackening that seemed like a burn from fire, and that blight first appeared on his right lower leg, until it discolored the entire leg. And when he saw the blight, he covered his leg, and it healed. But a long time later, the blight returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I applied counterirritants after purifying the flesh, but he could not stop the blight. He begged me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do so, as I had hope of mitigating the condition; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the man's strength was feeble. He became completely despairing, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed. And I have never heard of this happening again unless it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess should form in fat tissue, and it remains there for so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and perforates, causing the bowels to move, and staying within the flesh as if a vessel; and the skin covering is as delicate as fine cloth, and does not go down to the bone or nerve, and this disease is called 'sain' (abscess), and not 'fistule'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called 'fistule'; and the skin should be cut all around, especially when it is delicate, as with fine cloth; and its corruption should not be ignored.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you believe the skin is ready to heal and the corruption is not completely removed, and the skin is dry and stiff, then treat it with a warm cloth: check if the swelling is large, and the odor unpleasant; if so, use Egyptian medicine made as follows: take equal parts of salt, oil, litargyrum (a type of mercury sulfide), and place them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then, according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and apply it to the affected area, relaxing the opening; leave it for two hours, then remove it by straining; repeat this several times until the swelling is reduced and the impurity eliminated. If the patient cannot tolerate either Egyptian medicine or water from ashes (when the medicine is not available), gather ashes from vine shoots, mix them with water, strain, and use the liquid to clean the wound, until you are certain that it is thoroughly cleansed; however, if the opening is very small and the cloth used for cleansing does not fit inside, widen it a little using a hot iron, and apply some of the Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment (as described in the treatment of wounds) as long as there's enough space. If the wound is too large, and the edge cannot be moved by the cloth or water from below, then the opening is either at the top or bottom of the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow gas to form; and if you cannot cover the anus as you see fit, prepare in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest point it can, for when the bowel is perfect, it does not allow gas to form, and if you cannot cover the anus as you see fit, position it gently downwards, leaving no part of the bowel behind; and use consolatory medicines on the wound, covering it with a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then, as strongly as possible, close the gap in the side of the bowel slightly larger than the first, applying soft dressing to the other cloth according to the amount of the gap, and place it over the gap in the healthy part of the bowel to ease the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth outside for many days; and whoever is on top of the gap in the side of the bowel, often removes it to release the bowel, and knows what flows from the bowel, whether poison or pus or enough or digested or undigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when you see that the medicine has spread in this way over the gap in the healthy part of the bowel, then know that the wound is already healing, and brings health to it; and then release it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of health, for health draws near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those whose wounds do not heal until they have received treatment, and others who do the opposite; and if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open; and if the breast is slow to heal and remains so, then prepare medicines with moist substances in substance and dry in virtue, as a final remedy, for there is much vitriol in them, which is the last medicine; take this final ointment and mix it with rose oil and pour in old wine of equal substance; then preserve and use it; and do the same with cooked honey thickened; when the final ointment is not available, take mirra, aloe and incense, crush them and make a powder over the honey once it has been taken off the fire; then spread it on a cloth and apply it to the breast, and never administer alopecian or celestial lily roots, which are like flour and cornmeal; use simple or composite medicines: grind them and make a powder, and place it on the honey I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not heal, then know that corruption has taken hold, and made an impression in the bones, or hard members, or ligaments; as we said before regarding the cure for fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A pustule is an abscess that forms under a nail from the moisture in the hand, or foot, or perhaps in other parts; and when it becomes old and no attention is paid to it, it can lead to a serious abscess, causing pain and discharge until the root of the nail is destroyed, or even the entire nail. It causes corrosion down to the bone, resulting in strong, putrid odor, and the skin around the toe widens, turning a dark color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If, as we have explained in the previous section, you treat it and the treatment does not help, then you must remove all the excess nail material, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is clean; and if the nail catches a string and begins to prick, and the wound bleeds, it is necessary that you place the right under the nail that pricks the string, and pull it up, and gently and carefully cut off the string, and apply burning and corroding medications to remove everything; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see both corrupt, treat them as mentioned above, then cure until healed; and if it is frozen and swollen, and causes great pain, it must be treated first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the string beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain causes a deep ache in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The adjustment that is born in the hands of no one, by chance, is entirely flesh, and by chance, it has part where there are bones, and never a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or birth is in no way our fault.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which is born in no joint does not move, and that which is born in the joint of a joint may be stiff; the size of what is fleshy is very light, in this way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so hold him still.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born with or develops a dislocation, it is necessary that you first hold the joint firmly until the bone heals, then gently manipulate the bone to a suitable position, and finally treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come from pain in the joints come either from birth, or from a wound's healing, or from a burn, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary to close this wound, so that it must be repaired according to their natural forms, then place between two moistened cloths or drapes, oiled with rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or between two pieces of delicate cloth, as long as the wound is closed, as appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its fingers with the palm, then close the wound as appropriate.
des vils	Des vils" is not a complete or
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These veins are thickly wrapped, full of melancholic excesses, which come to many parts of the body; and there is more in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary for you to administer purgative medicines at times, and then care for the health of the basilic (vein).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of fire is according to two methods: one is with cups, and the black blood is drawn out; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is made according to this method: first, raise the leg with hot water very strongly until the flesh becomes tender, then pull the sick leg from above the ankle to the knee joint; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a large knife, then squeeze and draw out the black blood in your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure, and then tie it, and order him to let the flesh turn blue-black; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	One should raise the leg of the patient with the affected joint, if it has hair, then immerse it in hot water and raise it until it turns red and swells; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over fire, and then compress it on the vein at the base of the joint for a long time until it appears open. Then, cut the skin at the site of the vein, and scrape the vein from both sides until it is exposed, and it appears red and black, like a white thread; then pull the leg away from the wound, as much as possible, and compress it against the joint; then gently bend the leg towards another joint, and then compress again over three joints. Scrape the skin over the vein until it is exposed, and then raise the leg, as you have done before, and bend it to another joint, following the same method; then cut with a smaller size if necessary, and scrape, raising and bending until all the blood is drained, then finish by cutting. If you cannot drain it in this way, insert a needle through the entire thread, tie it, and pull while rotating your hand back and forth until the vein breaks; take care not to cut, because if you do, it will be impossible to drain or remove it, and harm the patient; once all blood is drained, place soft, moist wool over the wound, mixed with wine and rose oil, and dress it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if you see that it is contracted and twisted and wrapped up together, and it is not at all straight, as we have said, then it must be cut with a twist, but never tied; and treated as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to do it is to twist the vision tightly, but not cut, until the vein breaks; and it is of great severity, because if it were delicate, it would break the vein, but since it is thick, as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm regions where no plants or trees grow, and on land with no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere, from putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin, as if it were a serpent or worm winding itself among the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is characterized by a severe inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude forcefully, as if emerging like a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is opened, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it, from one and a half fingers' width up to two finger-widths thick, and leave the cloth on the leg. Whenever the opening widens, wrap the cloth around it again and the new opening; but if it gets too long, cut off a portion and wrap the remaining part, not cutting it at its base, until it is entirely drained; for if you cut it, it will retract into the flesh, causing abscesses and putrefaction. Therefore, it should be treated little by little, removing nothing from the body; and this vein, when opened, is as long as five or ten fingers, and I have seen it emerge in a man as long as one finger's width. When you cut it, if you make a deep cut or stab it, all the contents will come out. So it should be drained thoroughly, filling the wound with medicated herbs to prevent putrefaction for as long as necessary, then treat the abscesses accordingly.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never touch this vein again, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or hand, and a great wound occurs from it; treat it then as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and flesh. It spreads throughout the body, moving from one member to another, causing great pain as it breaks through the skin where it resides. It is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, snakes, leeches, and parasites in the belly. One doubts the severity of its ill effects, for when it moves through the body, it ascends to the head, reaches the eye, and sometimes retreats, destroying the eye. This happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done otherwise than when the pus has gone: therefore, you must lay the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it deeply, so that the pus flows out completely into the char (wound dressing), and you do not drain it again until it has healed; and the greatest harm it does is when it causes the oil to seep, as we have said; and if you see a swelling coming near the wound, first tighten the bandage around the eye's form (eyebrow), then cut and drain it forcefully; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification of the body with solvent medicines to eliminate harmful humors, and bathe in meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the breast; and after that, I noticed a little thing rising up on her shoulder, as quickly as anything could move, like a live silver coin when it cuts through flesh; the pain left that spot and moved to the shoulder, and then shortly afterward spread throughout the body, reaching the other breast; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had seen many times that the pain moved from one place to another, but I had never understood it as I did in this woman; and I thought that was because she had a dry body, her veins were exposed, and there was a certain constraint that showed itself; and I could not find any reason according to this perspective for those who are afflicted, having moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease cured and the patient feels that pain, as we have said, press it above and below gently, then squeeze until that constrained vent (or pressure point) on the body is released; and cauterize the wound; and if you do not have these at hand, cure it with what dispels the wind, such as foul pills, serpentum pills, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their appearance and the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that there are those with sharp, and small, and serrated tips, and some are smooth; and those with angles, and others with long ones, and those with pieces; and some that pierce any member do so in two ways: either in a principal member, like the head, body, liver, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it emerges in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterward, appears: it is necessary that you struggle with the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not entirely extracted, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow emerges and pierces the bone, and there is a sudden satisfaction felt on top of the brain, it appears as darkness and blinding and twitching and redness alone, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it comes out from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it loses speech and voice; and there is also a discharge of white pus-like matter from the wound, resembling wool, and also like foam from a horse. And if these signs appear to you, if you are skilled in treatment, pull out the arrow even if it is not fully embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow when it breaks or withdraws, is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were fixed in something hard, neither empty nor hollow; and by chance the arrow may also become silent like a pulse, and there appears black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never draws the pon (or perhaps: "and the sign that the arrow never draws back") is that there is no scum-free discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns color, and he breathes heavily and stops the pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces through the cover of the shoulder, it breaks small bones; and it inflicts great pain and causes sighing; and it moves all the muscles of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no healthy tissue left through which to pass it, then there is little hope for healing or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, the urine gushes out in spurts, and the patient feels intense pain; know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, as they feel and the pain in them, the neck and shoulder and elbow and hip and aid (support) and sharp pains in the back and stiff joints and the foot and legs, and any dislocated limbs or misaligned parts, are safe according to various arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck his eye at the root of the nose: I tried it, and removed it from the other side through the fat of the ear, and it was cured without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And at another time, an arrow struck in the fat of the eye below the paper, and the arrow was removed, leaving only the tip towards the wood, and it was a large arrow with a blue arc, very light without ears; the man was cured, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arabic arrow with ears: I shaved the beard, and slowly pulled it out until it came out, and the Christian was cured.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And take an arrow from the body, that was lodged in the stomach, and thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut through the arrow, extracted it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow lodged in his back or side, and the wound is deep; and the arrow remains stuck inside him, and he does not change his natural disposition, nor does he experience any harm from his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you will see another man, to whom an arrow has struck his face, and the wound is deep; he endures without suffering great pain; and many others similar to him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And he removed an arrow from the eye of the king, which had been shot into his nose, and it was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely extracted after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with great care, and felt nothing; but he experienced sharp pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of the arrow; I applied a soothing poultice to relax the muscles because they were cramped; and I could see the shaft of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the splint on tightly, and secured the wound from there, and thus the patient endured a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and it was removed.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound with firm hands until it healed and I tested it, feeling the tip of the arrow still stuck in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound using that medicine, until the point of the arrow became visible; it took over three months for the wound to heal completely, and then I used pincers to pull it from both sides, but it wouldn't come out; so I continued to try subtle and clever methods, until I found a set of well-made pincers, as described at the end of this chapter, and I pulled on it, opening up the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the greatest judges believe that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: so I restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows; so place your care on what I am saying, because books cannot fully convey it. But the wisest masters compare well very small things and new instruments, for the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are stuck, but according to two ways: either through the vein where they enter or from another place; and that which comes out by the side where it enters is an arrow that has entered into their flesh, and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it until the swelling around it subsides and becomes light; also, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days, and each day move it a little; and then it will jump, and if it doesn't, pierce through all the flesh with a very fine needle, until the swelling around it is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the top and goes all the way to one of the belly cavities near the brain, and none of the aforementioned accidents occur with the patient: do not pull it, but leave it until it becomes even after several days, for if the arrow stays there, it can be fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, and remains in the patient without further harm for some time, provided the skill of pulling it out is good.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply heat as I have told you; afterward, treat the bone while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.
