And if the arrow is withdrawn into the bone and one cannot see it, but feels it in every way; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound or because the arrow goes deep into the flesh where there are no bones, muscles, or nerves, then leave it until the wound is large enough; and pull the arrow as much as possible, and if it has roots on either side where you can, remove them so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let the limb rest around the joint until it is healed, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the symptoms of blood poisoning contradict what we have said about treatment in that chapter, then apply as we have instructed regarding the incision on the nerve and vein; and be wary of cutting into the arrow without danger, either immediately or later, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help, and if you cannot do so, then follow the signs that show you what to do.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another place, where it opens something within, causing the skin to swell in that area, both visually and through sensation: cut there, as much as the pincers can grasp, and then extract it: if it still feels sharp.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, widening it, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now and then try again until it comes out; and if the arrow is deeply embedded, let the entire shaft remain, and then apply pressure gently; if the tip of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument, push it out forcefully, and if the arrow is removed smoothly, insert the instrument with its tip entering simultaneously to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has pierced the skin, or the belly, or the bladder, or along the ribcage, and it is close to a vein or nerve, and you can cover it, do so; but beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and afterwards dress the wound, as required; and cure it until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The instrument used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak; here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape that points towards the tail is similar to a bird's feather, to push the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers for pushing and gripping, if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can draw blood, of which there are 16 main ones: 2 are the jugulars located behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the 2 arteries visible in the temples, and 2 veins in each arm, called "aspires"; the vein across the forehead; the vein at the crown of the head near the eyes; the 2 glands located on the collarbone; the 2 veins above the lips inside the mouth, called "augeherich"; and 2 veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins from which one draws blood are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side of the body and commonly called "vein of the head"; the median is called "close" (fast) and is composed of both the cephalic and basilic veins; the basilic is on the right side and is called "vein of the belly", and it lies beneath the femoral artery, being the one that appears most clearly when opening the vein.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the cure is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the knee from the left side, and the second at the ankle from the right side; and the third vein called 'nasse' which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of veins behind the ears aids in the cure of old catarrh and migraines. The quality of this treatment is that you raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then, you tie the patient's collar tightly until the two veins behind the ears become visible, hanging down from the head in two distinct parts. You should then apply pressure where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, which indicates the presence of blood flow. Take the lancet and make an incision just below the vein, up to the bone, then gently pull upwards on the entire vein against the flow of blood, making a cut through the skin and flesh and severing the vein properly. Let the blood flow out until you see it stop; then tie and bind it until it heals. I have already described incisions and cauterization in the previous book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, as they were old and dry, and the eyes accustomed to tears at their roots; and the quality of the healer is as I say: and it is that the patient holds his neck, as long as the two veins remain open; and he feels the pulse under his thumb on his right index, and then signs with a needle below, and gently presses the vein above, and cuts it, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to need; then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; then form the wound and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their excretion and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the health of the brain, as well as old facial diseases, and migraine, and redness; and its quality is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called 'denter', whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another instrument, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy and free from any broad cut.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, one should not let the flames be too intense; and the healthy hair should be cut at an angle, because the bone is close, and it might break the flame when it's thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The healthy hair from the two veins located in the arm is useful for healing wounds, pimples, redness, and eye inflammation, and facial diseases; its quality is such that the patient pulls their head tightly without any strain, as before. Then, cut it at an angle, neither too thin nor too thick, because there is no specific shape.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then apply pressure to the wound, as much as needed, and then bandage it, securing it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is worth much in treating a cold, sudden pain, and facial diseases such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, both new and old. The quality of the health is such that the patient tightens their jaw, strains their nose with their left hand, and inserts the subtle flame longwise between the two nostrils, since the vein does not open fully, and the blood will now begin to flow. Do not push too hard, and apply pressure with the sanc (presumably a type of medicine or treatment) according to your need, then bandage it for a night, as it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy water from two wells helps in the tightening of the eyelid, and at the beginning of sickness, and for many ailments, and for impetigo, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for boils; and the quality of the water is such that the patient pulls his lid away from both eyes, as we have said; and let the skilled one be on top of the sick person's head, and the sick person sits in a certain place, then clean the vein with long and wide strokes, then treat the wound with warm blood, as much as is needed; then do the same to the other vein, then unbind the bandage, and tighten the veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	from the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the lips helps to keep the mouth moist, and it aids in the healing of gum disease, lip cracks, and pain and swelling around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the veins is such that you make the patient sit before you, tighten their collar as I have said, then turn the lip, and examine both veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left; they are recognized because they are black, and also because they have small black veins around them: so cut each one, and if you do not know them or doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the veins that are beneath the tongue is a valuable procedure after the cleansing of the head, and it helps with throat tightenings, eye diseases, and mouth illnesses; the quality of the cleansing is such that the patient should feel the tongue move, gently pressing it down, and looking for any dark veins on each side. Then cleanse both, but do not press too hard as there are arteries beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat that are commonly cleansed are done in two ways: either by pressing with a hot flame at regular intervals, or with a fine, sharp tool (called an "anesil") as if cutting trenches, and they are wide and narrow according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the inflammation is very hot if it is much renowned, and it is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins with a flat, smooth instrument in places where there is much obvious blood clot, and which contain great blood clot and pus; and this is the shape of the olive-colored inflammation.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for healing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for diseases that are under the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the healer to heal gently, and to wash the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it touches the artery, and blood flows, if it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pressing, but cutting like iron.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and change it for another one; or if you want any part of it, heal it in place with a vein from another part of the body: it opens clearly; and cut it with iron flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you learn the vein of healing, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touch the vein until you know the pulse; then mark the spot with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with iron flame; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the vein swell, for that is the artery: flee from it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bubbling up from above like a child's urine, and the veins are red and tender, know that this is a sign of an artery: then quickly, place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger so that the vein does not burst, which often happens; let the arm be still and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins are not healed and they continue to bleed, and there is no medicine at hand, then press on the vein from its origin; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly to the other side; if it is not tired, that is good. If not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the binding is not too tight for the small size of the wound, nor does it cause any weakness in the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The treatment of the vein in the middle is helpful if it stops blood from the top and from inside, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer should wash himself by the nerve that is below, and if he does not clean it thoroughly, and touches the nerve, it swells and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person because of its subtlety, then you must treat it with an antiseptic instrument; and avoid touching the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if a vein is between the two bones, make it open long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for cephalica helps to draw blood from the head, and it aids the joints; and it is good to apply olive or myrrh flame, as it is the safest of all veins, for it does not contain any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is better to seek the lightest place, and do not be discouraged if it hurts the first time, and keep trying; and sometimes the veins may swell up in some men when they are punctured for the first time, but it does not hurt much.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should only be used to preserve health and prevent future ailments; and blood should be let in one of the three veins: namely, the cervical, femoral, or basilic vein. One should bloodlet at the beginning of prayer, after eating in summer and autumn, or in winter after two or three o'clock.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting used to treat illnesses does not have a specific time limit, but should be done as needed during the day or night; however, it is not advisable to bloodlet children under 12 years old, nor pregnant women for four months after childbirth until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old who have passed sixty years as ill.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to heal themselves in any way, it is necessary for them to clean out the intestines with a light enema, if they have much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw away from the excess of bad substances from the principal members; nor can one truly heal him who is too salt with meats or too greedy, as long as he remains thus; neither those who are sick from colic, vomiting, abdominal pain, frequent sexual intercourse, hard labor, wakefulness, or drinking and eating excessively; then, by subtlety, remove the humors, if they are excessive, either from foods, drinks, or medicines; if you have means to do so. Then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, in order to purify the blood, and heal the vein, as we have said, after the third day; and guard yourself that day against work, exhaustion, luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and consider yourself healthier than those whom you are healing; then rub your arm twice or three times; subsequently tighten the bandage in the middle, because if it is too loose, it cannot correct the problem; and then rub it with your hands until the veins swell and become warm. Then moisten the wound with a little old oil, and place your left hand's finger on the vein, below where you wish to heal it, so that the vein does not break or be injured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow as if they were strings in the body, and if they are of a type that are troubled by vapors, when fire is applied to them, the vein withdraws from the flame and cannot open, thus one suffers; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary that the healers be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, they must repeat this process a little further down on the same limb or elsewhere, for the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days and do not tie up the arm; perhaps abscesses will form later; do not enter the bath again, but resume treatment if it seems appropriate; and if the opening is small, carefully cut away the surrounding tissue subtly, without doubt, because this same opening can cause a great deal of blood to flow as you see in these cases. Do this a little bit more gently so that the vein becomes inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not immediately reopen the wound, but apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil becomes attached to this vein; thus administer the oil in each wound that you close the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done with triacs and bowels when applied to the vein; it soothes the pain and eases it when it is too hard.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms, which happens frequently, especially when the vein is not closed properly at first, hurry and apply a moist sponge with hot wool and hold it for an hour; after the blood flow from the vein stops, and if no black or green color remains in the wound after a few days, do not harm it; and if you see fit, apply aloe or myrrh mixed with calament juice, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appears at the wound of the basil (or holy) temple: so place your hand there, and if you feel the soft flesh under the pressure of your hand, then this is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So be careful not to apply anything that we have mentioned here, because it may dry out without reaching the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the flesh, then use another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its pain and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the pain is intense, let it flow as long as it remains red; and if you see it swelling, leave it to subside until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is strong and robust, and has the skill to extract blood, to make a wider wound and have larger flaps; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, making the incision smaller and more frequent, and one should clean the wound by cutting across, not by pricking. This method of cleansing prevents the spread of infection and nerve damage, and it is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body is afflicted with sickness, it is necessary to give a moist drink of pomegranate juice; if he is heated, he should take bloodletting three times or four. And if he has a cold complexion, he should eat before the sickness a moist drink of muzzled syrup, or syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and fennel, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints from sickness, after the release of much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a steam of bread soup and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to remove his arm, or heal it another time, as needed, when it is weakened by much blood letting, he should heal it little by little, according to the amount of its continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to remove his arm after the first blood letting, and he has strong stiffness, he should heal it after seven hours from the first blood letting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another place, he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body, which has been heated, and causes fever; it needs to be drawn out in large quantities, and the opening widened as much as possible until it closes of its own accord; then you must consider all conditions of health, and place your hand upon the pulse when it strengthens, so that death does not come in its place, and this often happens when healing is neglected; and it is wrong to, when you see the arm loosen, and cause blood to flow again, and the opening close, press firmly on it; nor if it is curved, should you force it straight, for that would be harmful; but leave it until it heals again on its own; or you can gently apply a pointed flame to the tip of the fire, until the coldness in the vein opens, and put some thread soaked in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, leave it alone and do not press on it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw off the blood again because of the abscess, either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of the vein is that the patient should bend his hand in hot water until the veins become red, then tie it slightly so that the vein appears well, and now draw the blood through it, not too wide or too narrow; and make the opening wide at the joint of the hand, and do not let any pus escape, and put the hand back into hot water and let the blood flow in the hot water until you have enough; and if this is the case, do not stop bending the hand in hot water, because it is put into greater heat than necessary; and the vein from which the blood is drawn is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the salvation of the hand on the right side is good for all ailments of the flesh, and this is the manner: stretch the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein is engorged, if you see it; and if the wound is across, and if you touch every part with it, nothing should grieve; but do not press too hard, for the nerves are entirely exposed, and then return the hand to hot water, if it feels numb in the wound, and it cannot issue forth.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and silk to seal the wound tightly, and so do with every person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person grasps the mouse with the left hand to treat the disease of the eye, and does everything as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sage of the soul grasps all diseases emanating from the body, such as illnesses of the marriage (possibly referring to reproductive issues), retention of flowers (perhaps a metaphor for urinary problems), diseases of the rain (a possible reference to hydrocele or swelling), old joints and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health is such that the patient immerses himself in hot water and rubs the vein until it bursts, binding it over the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot, it flows with much blood; healthy then, or a larger flow of blood, or at the ankle, where it most moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it on the foot, be careful not to touch the bones, and clean it just as when you cut; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the wound will not heal, immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the dressing is needed for the first time, repeat it slightly higher the next time, because the bones are salt; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same thing with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's ankle, and its health corresponds to the pain in the back when it's filled with hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its health is such that the patient feels pain in the bath, and three turns above the ankle are required to extract it, as otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, the health flows freely in all ways, passing through; and it moves like you would cup it, for the lion is safe, and it is greatly aided by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not draw it, no rain of health flows from the vein that opens on the back near the small toe, and be careful not to tighten the bandages; and make sure the blood does not escape, and then untie the knot, and put cotton and tighten; now it is healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	From the suction of the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or iron, or glass; and the suction is created in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This suction, performed without striking, is done in two ways: either it is hot or cold; and the suction created by drawing blood and extracting it from veins is carried out in twelve parts of the body: first, all over the head; then, between the collarbone; next, on both sides of the neck; under the jaw; on both shoulders; on both legs; on both ankles; and finally, on both feet. The suction should not draw blood from any major veins, only from small ones scattered throughout the body, so as not to weaken anyone excessively, just like with a vein-sucking treatment; it is not appropriate to perform such suction in cases of overfullness, while the entire body remains empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness or custom it is required to purge, each hour in the beginning and end of the month, and at every time; for there are such who, when they need to purge, have a heavy head; and some who experience bloating and redness in their face, and on their head, and down their neck, and darkness as well; and such who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and vomit blood; and there are even those who dream and see blackness, nausea, pain, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order purging after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon of the muscle finds aid in the heat of the chief ...  which comes from itself, and it is not right that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this application is to the health of the head, and it is not appropriate for those with a cold complexion or scabs, as it does them much harm; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold headaches.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who use this treatment often, it can become obstructed, and for this reason, a suction cup should be placed slightly lower out of doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for the health of the heart and lungs, and due to its constriction, it causes pain in the throat, and tightness in the channel of the windpipe, and sometimes, and bloating; and it should be relieved, because if it clings too tightly, it obstructs the nose and stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation of the chest as it affects the ribs in the neck can cause headaches, eye pain, and migraines, as well as choking and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is opposed to the health of the veins in the basilic; and you should instruct the patient to gently press his hand against the area, without pressing on the artery, to avoid complications with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammation of the gums is beneficial for mouth diseases, and for the corruption of the gums, and similar ailments in the mouth; it is located in the area of the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The inflammation of the cuts is as beneficial as three veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins; and instructs the patient not to squeeze too hard, for the flesh is devoid of strength, and knows how to close and open arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The vacuum that is on the thigh is as useful for draining pus from the depths, and for treating internal illnesses, and it should be large and made of iron, so that it can effectively draw out; and if it is too delicate, it might break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg vacuums should be applied firmly because they draw blood from throughout the body, and they are as effective as ancient remedies for rheumatism, kidney pain, and bladder problems, and they remove fluids; and they are used on the second ribs and the two ankle joints, but after prolonged use, they weaken the body and cause greater discomfort.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first, place it on the skin while empty and suck gently, then apply it firmly and move it evenly without ceasing until you see the red and swollen veins appear, opening the channels of blood; then release, and apply cups again, taking care in their arrangement, for some have very tough skin and clear pores. It is only necessary to strike once, and make wide incisions, and quite deep; suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: first, to open the thick channel of the large vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very intense, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to drain blood little by little, we are satisfied with doing so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must do this often; and if the pain is intense, striking with precision until the vessels are suddenly pierced, it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have porous pores, to apply oil from suction cups that is both opening and dissolving: in this case, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is cold, chard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar herbs.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a skin that is tender and has large pores, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but instead, they should wash it after the application of rosewater, cold water, water from morelle (a type of cherry), water from a cucumber, water from porcelain, or any other similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have excessive moisture, should rise from it using myrrh water, sumac water, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess weight should rise from old wine, or holy water, or a decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a cupping glass before or during a bath, but rather after the bath, an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that they wash themselves, when and where they need to be cupped and after being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be careful that those who are sick with colic do not eat things that are too hot and spicy; it is advisable for them to consume cold foods such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce, and similar things; also eat little, avoid chili, and opt for moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion should imbibe syrup of honey and fragrant wine, somewhere between old and new, and eat small portions, and eat little birds and pigeons; and on the day that he takes cold, he must drink more than he eats; and it is appropriate to give any man at any time triacle or musk before or after the chills, in order to strengthen the principal limbs; but it is not advisable for those who are hot to consume it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and intestines and joints, because these members do not tolerate injury from heat, and they are only used to draw blood from one member to another, as we apply them to the mammary glands when nursing; to remove the viscosity from a member, as we use suction cups on the stomach and bowels to reduce the member; and it removes pain, in cases of congestion or stones, perhaps by drawing away the congestion or expelling the stone from its place; and thus it acts when applied to the liver and spleen with retained wind, and these suction cups are left empty to suck only; and they should never be heated together, nor filled with cold water as in cases of tears, but rather they are filled with hot water infused with suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered by fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have two parts as wide as a palm and a half, and on its edge around the middle, it should have a small hole, no bigger than to fit an needle, and it must be made of steel or iron, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and it should have a crossbar of the same material, either steel or iron, to hold a cloth, and their sizes vary according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the suction cups for infants are different from those for adults, and for thin people than for fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup over the limb: take the wax or linen cloth, and put it through the hole in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cup, preventing it from burning the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you look, the steam goes out, and remove the suction cup; and take the linen cloth as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is administered for pleurisy, or any acute condition, it has no hole or opening, and can only be applied when it is filled with water, and placed on the limb only briefly; its shape is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without any wounds that can be treated with cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in the naked parts of the body, like the anus or nipples, or other similar places; and if the quality of the wound is such that when you find a cup that is in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, take it; and place it in sweet water until they become relaxed, and have nothing in their stomachs; then clean the wound and cup, and rub the member until it turns red, and apply the cups; and when they are painful and screaming, if it is a part where cups can be applied, then apply them, for this is much better afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the lion does not rise from its sleep, and then water is drawn out well and the wound is bandaged; and if the wound heals too soon after the removal of the bandage, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, place it on top, until the wound is completely healed; and if the wound multiplies, apply vitriol or gall, or similar substances, until it is healed; or you can put half-peeled fèves on the lion, leaving them there until they adhere to the wound, which will heal it. If more are needed, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not want to be taken, rub fresh blood on the lion, or insert an needle into the wound until it bleeds, and then place them back; and soon as they smell the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are detaching, sprinkle a little aloes and silk powder, or ash, and they will stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear pupil, that the wise eyes of this chapter flow from a source unseen in any ancient book; nor did anyone ever read or write about it. For this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good thereof; and I know nothing of it except by the learning of ancient books, whereon I have so diligently studied that I have acquired knowledge through experiment and the custom of my life. And here I have described to you what is contained in this chapter, abridged at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we should begin this prologue of this book by explaining the words and chapters where the wise apply their minds to truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture, dislocation, or twist occurs, it is necessary to quickly tend to the patient on both sides. If nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the affected part is too close or too cold, and you avoid cold things like ice, and meat from birds and squirrels, and do not drink wine, nor consume fatty foods, and do not overfill the veins with meats that fill the vessels with blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess forming, hot or spreading of material to the member; then return the patient to his former state as he had used to be.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one alleviate the patient from foods that cause excessive flatulence, or have a viscous quality, such as cooked flour in water, and laughter, and talking, and pressure, and the distension of the belly, and gases, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive flatulence, if it recurs and the fracture persists,
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the very old and decrepit cannot be well healed or fused according to their nature for the preservation of the limbs, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but take no heed, reset the broken bone with strong grips that join the member together, as it was before, without moving it entirely, and for this reason, satiate it with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, such as the edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and the fracture is a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type of dislocation has its own mechanism and specific instrument for restoration, according to the nature of the injury; the fracture of the bone is known because the joint is twisted and opens widely when pulled away, and it feels solid under pressure from the hand. But there is no fracture if there is no twisting or crack or slight dislocation; it can only be a twist, or a split, or a minor dislocation.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply medications that will be described later; then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that occurs in the joint, where the two parts are separated, you must now bring them together evenly so that the abscess can form properly; and if the abscess appears hot, leave it for some time until it cools down; then position it even, gently and carefully, and know that the restoration of a dislocation without broken bones is easier than restoring a fracture with pieces; then pull it as appropriate.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into pieces, and it extends from two parts, whether it's the hand or foot, or one of the small members, or at two joints, or at a joint and your hand; place the member according to its natural form, so that when the severed parts of the member are aligned, rearrange them using all available means until they return to their proper positions, and take care not to cause the patient further injury or pain through your actions; adjust both halves of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it feels well in the hand, but you think it is not properly aligned: dress it nicely, do not tighten it too much, and do not press as those who, through their actions, cause abscesses, heat, and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is completely still, gently apply warmth to the patient so that he does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor in any other way; and take care that the limb remains completely at rest so that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it means that the limb is completely still, and you should then put it into a position where it does not feel any pain; and be careful that there is no curvature when restoring it, and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the damaged member can be various in smallness and greatness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because it has small members, as arms and legs and similar: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and thin linen; and those that are larger, like the thigh and leg: they should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire large member, and tightens it equally from all sides, so that there is no gap; then add lighter bandages, three or four turns according to the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the whole bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, as the break gradually moves away; and soften the bandage little by little, until you press a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage and turn it again over the broken place; then return to the part below the break, and tighten it moderately, neither too hard nor too soft, as we said in the first chapter above; then insert between the thick bandages made of linen or cloth, until they are all even, then tie everything on top with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, apply a hot, soothing compress to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it for several days; then stretch your arms and legs, and use a narrow cane cut sharply from a sturdy branch or palm frond, shaped as follows.
