mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the stick that is placed on the fracture should be slightly thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large. Then tighten the sticks as you did in the first layer, and tie them together with a thread, as was done in the first layer on the fracture; the threads should be tighter at one end than the other, but not too tight or too loose; and the thread should be made of fine flax, for if it is too thick, like twisted flax cords, it is a great error, because the bandage will not be even if it is too thin, and it is not appropriate for there to be less space between each stick.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pain from the stars after dislocating them in their healthy joints, he should place soft compresses or other rags over them so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the blood vessels are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the stars of the fractured members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not appropriate to put stars inside until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the hot swelling; and see here the ancient method of applying plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this preparation, not too liquid or too thick, and use it; this is the common way of using a plaster to restore fractures in many positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for repairing fracture and dislocation and torsion: take hare's feet and lamb's flesh and onion and asafoetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each 3 parts; mirra and aloe, each 5 parts; ales (alums) 7 parts; make it into a powder and mix with egg white; if the man's body temperature is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones severely, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for torsion: take myrrh and wormwood, each 3 parts; mirra and aloe, each 5 parts; hawthorn 6 parts; Armenian powder 10 parts; grind well and mix with water or egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to splint joints and straighten bones out of their sockets, easing the pain that comes with it, is by using a new cloth, moistened in hot oil or wine, and placing it over the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and neatly extracting the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to splint broken bones: take dry fig leaves and fresh poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to ease the return of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of chamomile, camomile flowers, violet flowers, and wheat flour, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and apply to the affected member, heating it. Alternatively, mix with fresh coriander water or water. Use as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering for the restoration of a member when a hard abscess forms.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of alder, flax, balm, melilot, and chamomile, and flowers from violets, all in equal parts; grind them and macerate with sharp salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not apply heat or cold directly to a broken member, but rather a certain mixture made of wax and oil, nothing else, and it should be neither too hot nor too cold.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	Galen seems to suggest that one should apply warm, dry substances to a broken member to aid in healing, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective against injury and pain: take moss and sheep's hair or feathers from an owl, or the down of a bird, and mix them equally, grind them into a paste, and use it as a plaster and secure it with a bandage.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, release the plaster carefully and take care that the patient does not feel any pain or that the bones do not move from their place; if pain comes back or itching, or swelling appears, act quickly, remove the plaster, and take away the bandage now; take a light cloth and a sponge with moist sea water, dip it in water or rose oil, and apply it to the affected area for as long as the itching stops and the pain is calmed; then let the limb rest for an hour, and then cover it with dry linen moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it tightly until you are certain of the heat of the abscess. And thus, continue the treatment gently, using a little more plaster, and do not tighten it as strongly as before; apply it subtly until it heals completely.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful, and swollen, and it recurs, then you need to apply a plaster and bind it, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not heal after what we have said for three, four, five, or seven days, and it does not leave the dislocation for twenty days until the fracture heals and the adjustment of the bone to the flesh is close, then you hold it more tightly than before and fatten the flesh as I have said above; and if you see that the limb dries out more than necessary, know that healing will not come. Therefore, apply warm water each time you loosen it, every third day, and open a little the wound; by this work, thus cuts off the source of the malady to the limb, and it is shameful that foolish people prolong the dislocation in such a way: it is harmful and very dangerous, and I see nothing else but to let it heal and do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fracture, with various shapes and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the bone breaks completely through to the other side, as with a hatchet or axe; and this type of fracture is called "hatchet-like.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and these two types of fractures can be either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a shock or compression, or a crack from stone or from a blow on stone, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture that approaches the skin just beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is caused by a stone or a blow or any similar thing, and a piece of bone enters inward, and the bone ends are aligned like a blacksmith's anvil when he was forging on the anvil; if the piece of bone gets stuck inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those who have moist heads, such as an infant's head; and it happens in all these ways of dislocation that smaller parts are broken off, as if they were; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations due to traction on them, and the inquiry at each joint, and by the corrupt flesh above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known because when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it thoroughly, the dislocation becomes apparent from the open black mark.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any harmful incidents, such as vomiting, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, ague fever, or other symptoms appearing in various combinations, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it happens that you hastily remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the wound beneath the bone is corrupted, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks down to the tissue covering the brain, it is necessary that you cut the broken part in this way: and you must press the patient's head gently, and expose the bone in every way possible, and clean the wound more softly than you can, and if a discharge of pus comes from exposing the bone, or abscess at the base, you should use the aid that is appropriate, and fill the cavity with moistened rose oil cloth, and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be assured of no further discharge. Then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two methods: one way is that you cut a narrow channel in front, and this is its form...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another method even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different sizes of threads, some twisted and others broad, and they are sharp and made of indurated iron; and you work gently so as not to damage the surface.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, you need to drill around it, using threads with intervals, so that they do not go through the bone too deeply, and there should be a margin or a circle on top of the point, preventing it from going beyond the bone; and you will need many of them, so that each one comes in its proper place according to the thickness of the bone, allowing for threads throughout; and this is the form of the three types of threads:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to know if an bone is broken is that you place pressure on it and return your hand to its normal position until you are sure the bone is dislocated; then put pressure somewhere else a little later, and so on around, then cut away the space between the cracks in the bone with incisions, and do this as delicately as possible, while still holding the bone firmly in your hand or using any tools like pliers or tweezers. Be careful not to touch the brain or the soft tissue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have dislocated and treated the bone, it is necessary that you feel the tension remaining in the bone compared to all other tools resembling an incision tool, but it must be more delicate and subtler than any other incision tool; and if it holds onto small bones or scales, gently remove them with the appropriate instruments. Then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a portion of the bone, either by opening the fracture widely, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place the tip of this curved scalpel beneath it, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on the second side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet, carefully copping the bone all around, and be very mindful of the skin that lies beneath; if it is away from the bone, lift it slightly, for if you remove it too closely, it will cause great pain and harm.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the flesh, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to file off the roughness again, and remove the scales with a delicate rasper in which you must have various quantities, so that each part can be made as convenient as possible according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulty with raspers, and then with more subtle ones, do not cease from this task until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to make adjustments according to their location; and this is something that cannot be fully answered by anyone who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the patient is satisfied with the exposure, it is necessary that you cover the wound with a cloth, according to its size, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as gently as possible so as not to harm the patient, then apply another bandage, and do not tighten it too much until the abscess has healed completely; leave it like that for a day or two, until the abscess is calm, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vetch, incense powder, aristol, and similar things; make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer universal remedies without burning; be sure that the wound remains clean, and do not leave any dressing or pressure on it, for when bowing gathers on the skin of the head, it erodes and damages, and causes great harm to the patient, because when a biting substance is placed on the syph (abscess), it hardens by itself.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no ill accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine placed upon it, to see if it has any virtue, it is necessary that you mix a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and a drape of glue, and place it over the wound; then cure it in the manner of cures as it should be, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the bones above are never broken, either together or separately, for they are two bones; and the middle part is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your small finger or a narrow tool between the joints, and place the break back into its natural position, and hold it there until the joint returns to its original form; do this gently, and ensure the patient feels no pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot reach it, you must place a slightly thicker rod at the top of the joint to hold it in place until the pain subsides.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, do as I said before, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, wait until the seventh or tenth day after the swelling has subsided, then place thin linen strips over the joint, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken, and make it whole; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the gaps in the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required to moisten the bandages with butter, and to change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good enough, but it is advisable to moisten them with egg yolk and mill powder, then leave the bandage until the bone is hard and the cartilage stiffens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one apply goose fat in place of other remedies, and if the wound is covered with pus, hold the break still, and let the patient breathe; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form at the site of treatment while you are working on them, apply a mixture of wax and oil or a poultice of duck fat.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not drain from the site of treatment, apply a poultice made of flour and incense powder, confited with egg yolk, then place light bandages on top and do not tie the neis; and if the break in the neis is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them using suitable instruments, then clean the wound with hot charcoal and ointments, and cover it with clean bandages and splints until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly out of place, and not broken in two, but a support from within holds it together, if one knows it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger of your left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert your index finger of your right hand, gently pushing the fracture inward, then pull it out with your other hand, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is severe in two parts, you must administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth causes a fracture, or if it is held in place by a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply cerate to the broken mandible and place a double cloth over it; and on top of the cloth, put a large, well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and secure it with ties as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, on the third day, then reset it so that it is changed; and apply a poultice of powdered flour with plenty of egg or sesame flour after removing the bandage; and place a thin covering poultice, if the poultice hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until he is healed; often he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses occur, then apply as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, do not remove any piece of the bone that is broken; carefully remove the instruments suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and it does not delay, immediately close the wound if it is wide, and place suitable plaster on it to draw out the poison, as long as it remains healthy.
de la forcele	of the force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force often breaks in several places, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is of three kinds: it may be completely broken, with fragments, and is the easiest to restore; or it may involve a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is as follows when there is a fracture without a wound, that you have two helpers, so that one holds the part that is strongly broken, and the other stretches the collar towards the affected area; then put the fracture back in place with equal measure, so that its form is as it should be, and there is no deformity or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round, thick cloth or woolen spike under the patient's shoulder, according to your need; stretch and gently apply force, hold the spike in your hand, and put the fracture back in place as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out, because it comes out completely, then it is necessary that the patient lies on his side with his arm below, and the healers raise the shoulder upwards, until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary that you cut through it; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join together in any way, use the forceps as a support to hold it in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should resemble a spoon, and is not too sharp, but as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the force required for the operation; it has two edges, as you can see, one wider and the other narrower, corresponding to the rupture of the wound that you made when you worked on the bones; and when you are certain of the hot aposteme, if the wound is deep, use bandages and gauze, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, take a cloth moistened with rose oil, and silk, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straining of the bone, when it has wounds and cuts, is that you place on the bone the plaster of very fine powder and egg albumen, and put light bandages on top, and insert a spear under the bandage, if needed; then take a very wide strip of cloth, about a palm in width, and place the drape over the bandages and plaster; then take a thin, long ribbon three times as wide as it is long, and wrap it around the cloth, so that the edge of the cloth hangs down; put the ribbon on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder; and rearrange each part, and when you see that the bandages hold firmly on the fractured bone, and you clearly see that the ribbon does not move from it, rewarding each day, and when the stitches loosen, so adjust; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small cushion under the injured shoulder while he sleeps; this lightens the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or binding the arm to the chest, and do not loosen it if no bad accidents come for twenty days; then repeat the plastering, if needed, and tighten and leave it thus until it is healed; and it is healed in no more than twenty-eight days, and less for most men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated, it does not immediately return to its normal position and can only be corrected by touch; if you arrange it according to the form of the dislocation, and restore it to its natural state in every way possible, then sprinkle a little fine powder on it, apply light bandages, and cover with a double cloth. Then place a broad and thin board, slightly wider than the shoulder, and adjust the board so that it covers all parts of the shoulder; use strips of linen for this, ensuring the board is even. Tighten a strong bandage around it, so that the board does not move from its place, and inspect it every day. Whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and if the board shifts, return it to its correct position, having the patient lie on his side. The shoulder can be restored in 20 or 25 days, and when this time is up, carefully remove the bandage, as it is not a bone that returns easily to its place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not removed from the inside, it pushes up and the bone, and does what we have said about calming the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the breaking of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fracture is never broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; but it often breaks at the extreme.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken at the extreme, it declines inward and the patient feels great pain, and there is no improvement, and sometimes it bleeds, and opens up the joints in the broken bone, and it feels better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with both hands, and gently adjusts it in all ways as necessary so that the bone figure is correct; then apply plaster and compresses over the delicate salt or other light cloth, wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so it does not move; and tighten the bandage regularly on the back, and adjust it closely, and check the freedom every hour, and if it softens, tighten it; and if it needs to be released due to corrosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly, loosen it, remove the plaster, and address the cause of the issue; then reapply the plaster and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to the patient during examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you place the fracture back in its proper position, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the splint, securing it with a stick, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inclining inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as if from crying out, because the bone pierces the flesh; and it causes numbness in the fingers, and sometimes vomiting, great weakness from blood, and it is a serious illness, and the old ones have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is necessary to administer foods that cause bloating in the belly to drive out the fracture from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that incisions without heat will not come if they have not previously been caused.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, as long as it is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of you should apply cupping glasses to the skin, as it forms a vacuum, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cup might draw away excess fluids from the body due to weakness in its position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the wound with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the space around it, then treat the cure for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the broken bone, then doubt is in the patient, and it is necessary to cut into the ribcage, and place an instrument to stop the bleeding; and then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with bandages, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, place moist, oil-soaked cloths on the affected area and lay down; and treat while the abscess is present, keeping the patient lying on their side where it hurts, until they heal.
de la brisure dou col	from the breakage of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No break occurs in the collarbone bone, and seldom does it happen without rain; also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if they will recover, be wary if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and unable to move or stretch them; if you pierce them with a needle, they should not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, if they remain silent and feel well when pressed and not moved, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar symptoms occur in the back and you want to know if it is a sign of healing or not, be careful if the pain is relieved, and if there are movements that cause discomfort, especially when coughing or sneezing; and when it is remembered on the belly, there is frequent egestion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered on the back and it wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is fatal: therefore, do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess, apply warm rose oil or egg-white oil to it until it is soothed; then place a comforting and drying plaster on it, secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where the pain is felt until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it should be covered with a bandage; then the bone is removed, and the two edges of the wound, if large, are sutured with stitches, and treated with healing ointment diligently until it heals; and if the fragment of the bone, known as the "fragment of the break," is stuck in your hand, you should hold it with your left hand and place it level with the other hand, then apply the plaster and splint if necessary; then tighten it, and if there are any separated bones, reduce them and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the bone of the spine
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the spine is fractured, and if there is no slight reduction at the site, it causes prolonged, declining pain to the patient, along with stiffness, swelling, and aching where the fracture is.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it as long as you are above the fracture site; and know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then apply equal pressure until it regains its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it bends inward, so place the patient on his belly until the healing of this fracture becomes visible.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place a splint on it, then put a piece of wood or hard material over it and tighten the fracture so that it does not move; and hold the limb away from the body until the bone is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, it should be calmed down until the abscess has healed, and apply what we have said above; then return to restoration, tighten it as needed, if there is no adverse event, and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joint (ajutoire) is that which connects the collarbone to the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, then it should be restored using one of two methods: one involves taking a wooden stick, roughly medium-sized, shaped in this manner:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two feet together, and turn them upwards, and place the patient on his back; then stretch out one broken arm onto the leg, until it becomes relaxed, and fasten a piece of wood across it, then press down on some heavy object or have the assistant pull it downwards; then take both hands and make the break even, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that we place the patient on his side, and bind one hand to his neck, then command the assistants to each take hold of a part of the broken bone in his hands, and stretch them out to their respective sides.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too forceful, then tighten the ligature around the rupture, and on the rupture, extend each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the rupture is close to the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to place a moderate ligature below the joint, and another towards the throat, below the rupture; and if the rupture is towards the throat, a light ligature should be placed without strain, as long as the rupture remains balanced on its place, then set the rupture correctly and tighten it, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms again after it has been extracted and doesn't subside for seven days or more, apply a moist cloth dipped in rose oil to the wound until the abscess is calmed; then extract it, and the manner of extraction is such that you place a splint on the dislocation, then reassemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; then cover with a bandage, and extract the splint from the dislocated joint and the arm, so that the arm is held in place by the bandages, provided nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt whether the bone has moved and use splints, place a wider and stronger splint on the dislocation than the others, and ensure there is two fingers' width space between each splint, and make sure each splint is so large that it covers three-quarters of the dislocation, as we have said at the beginning of this chapter about the dislocation. Then extract the splints, stronger and closer together.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, when you restore the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it bound for up to seven days, as we have said; then every three days check the binding, ensuring no inflammation arises or comes to the place, so that healing can come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the condition improves, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such incident occurs, and it is not until after three days or more that the binding is removed, then have the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place under the dislocated member a flat cushion of equal thickness wool, and every hour watch during the day or night to ensure the dislocated limb does not move or become loosened. If it recovers through the power of medicine and follows the diet we previously described, then gradually make the food more substantial when it begins to improve.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the joint and leg should be taken up again after forty days from all movement; and then one must dislocate and apply baths and medicinal oils to direct the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and tight, it may take up to days or two months to dislocate.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosse," of which one is small and follows the wrist; and the other is large, and is below the small bone towards the hand. Perhaps only the large bone is broken, or perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration is light and swift, but when the large ones break, recovery is poor and more difficult than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, they should be gently extended and aligned evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, they should be pulled stronger; stretch them on a cushion, and place the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower, and let the patient cross their arms over themselves, with the cushion in front of them higher than their pain will allow; then have another minister stretch the other arm towards the joint of the hand or further up, and another at the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then arrange them evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture, each one is placed in its proper position, and if there is none that catches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, making a cut above and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a specific chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration there are abscesses, I apply a bandage made of oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft, and I wrap it gently until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and apply the pouder made of very fine flour with plenty of egg, then place the needles, making the needle from the rupture stronger and slightly wider than the others; know that there should be six needles or more in various positions: if the rupture is in one bone or in two; tighten more over the rupture than elsewhere, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and make the cloth lying on the rupture soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, from which it is drawn, be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse event occurs in the limb, such as itching that arises in the member, then you should immerse the limb in hot water until the itching is soothed; and allow the member to rest without compression.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the process, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones move out of place, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if inflammation cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you should loosen it slightly and leave it for a few days until the swelling goes down, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said help the patient, then let him rest for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, bind his hands to his chest, making sure the collarbones are even, and guard against movement and gesture, and have him sleep on his back. Know that this fracture will be healed in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, depending on the combination and disposition of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and between the fingers, there are many small fractures, which come about through frequent pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the hand's bone is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to cut across it and make it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface and extends the broken bones' ministers, and adjusts them level, as much as they are well joined; and applies a poultice and blisters if an abscess does not come, and then he wraps it with a piece of linen cloth according to its size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the side of the hand near the stomach, make a ball of cloth and instruct the patient to press it against his broken hand; then pull it with a long piece of cloth, and wrap it tightly with a heart-shaped soft cloth as large as the hand itself.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the end of a bone, you should place one stick above and another below on the base, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it firmly around the hand, and stop the blood flow between the two sticks.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in neither of the joints, and it is a break, place it evenly, as it should be, and tighten it with the base, and if you see that it needs a small, straight stick to stabilize the break, do so, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in other joints, like the index or any of the others, place it evenly and tie it with the healthy joint that follows; you can either hold them all at once, which is better, or put a stick on top, as needed; and be careful during the restoration and alignment of the bone, supporting what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hipbone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its place in front and behind; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break, and another piece below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each limb extends its muscle equally; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one of the muscles should be bound towards the knee, and the others bound below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then loosen the ligament of the knee and extend it downward; then place the splint so that the bone is level in both hands, according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bind it, so that the lump does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap the fracture with a hard bandage, twice in two or three layers, and remove any excess; then turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and tie it tightly above; then return to the leg and thigh, wrapping the bandage again; then apply a splint with stars, and place a star over the leg bone; then use eight layers of soft cloth between the leg and thigh to ensure even compression, and begin binding in three or four turns around the splint; the tighter you go above the splint, the less it restricts movement; then take the two threads you passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three stars on top; then return below the knee with the thread, until you reach the sole of the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, leave it like that, and in no case should there be any abscess or swelling or other issues.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, and he dislocates it, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that stick, if one can, then do so; and if one cannot, it is necessary to break the joint and pull it out forcefully; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the foot be broken in this way as it is done for the hand or arm; however, the patient does not recover from the pain after such restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 to 10 days, or even less or more, according to the variety of complexes.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the street of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or a gap, it becomes an opening to all wounds, and feels pain, and this feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put things back in their proper place as much as possible, then apply a poultice, and place a round bandage if needed, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, like an abscess high up or any similar thing; apply what is suitable for each case, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, which are called "right" and "frosty"; and every fracture occurs as it does in the arm, and the treatment is similar, with all the same difficulties. And if both bones are broken together, the leg can move in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well, and it turns outward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer an extension, and set it evenly, and tie the stars equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are several pieces where the extension should be less and lighter; and straighten according to your ability.
