Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth that are dyed red and wrap them around the leg from one side to the other, extending from the knee to the ankle; then wrap two more bands above and below, and tie them in the middle, so the leg cannot move to the right or left, and thus it is well. And no one should administer any treatment along the length of the leg, but if it is made of cloth, they put the leg in a position to prevent movement, and they properly treat the fracture where there is an abscess or any other accident; they move the leg each day to see if there is any pus or other complications, and they cure it as long as it remains healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the fracture of bones in the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the joints dislocated in various ways, without force in most cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them stacked on top of each other, the patient will cry out with great pain on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then place your foot on his, raising the bones; then press it so that they return to their proper places; then apply a splint and bandages above, and under the belly of the foot, a small, flat table with two holes, then tighten it well around the foot, wrapped in cloth and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, but they are dislocated, as we have said about the hand's joints, then take a stick according to the length of the bone and make it slightly wider, then place this under the foot, firmly securing it; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, put on each one a stick according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen bandage, and secure the table under the foot; and let it be firmly attached at the top of the table towards the stomach of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, when we have spoken; and treat each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	fracture of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling subsides, then she should tilt her body to one side with the injured arm behind her. Next, fill the palm with cotton and place a heavy object on top; then have her stand up and gently rock her back and forth, allowing the cotton to enter the fracture site until the bone returns to its original position. After this, replace the cotton and repeat the process for seven days or so. If successful, the fracture will be healed and she can use her hand again. If necessary, take a bladder of goat's hair, tie one end to the opening, and squeeze all the air out into the injured area; then let it deflate naturally. The nature of the fracture will heal; fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is cured.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand or the woman's bone is broken, restore it as we have said regarding the hipbone; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and skill into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates various dispositions for restoration; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the staff is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the staff; then wrap rags around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals completely.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For those with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the shin or shoulder or similar, it is important to seek immediate medical attention, so that the healing process can begin, as we have discussed.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still vitriol present, and you have no other options, then begin to reset the fracture in the same hour or day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess appears again, leave the healing until it is completely healed, and do not touch it for at least a day or two, otherwise you might cause further harm.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible upon uncovering the heart, it is necessary that you gently place your hands on it with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear even when placing your hands, take this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight fingers in length (or according to the width required for the wound), and adjust it precisely; it should be round and slightly thicker so that it does not bend under pressure upon the limb during your treatment, and wider at the front, thicker in the middle, like so:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," so it is necessary that the broken bone be placed on top of the visible joint; and hold it in place once, until it returns to its original position, and becomes even on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instruments cannot securely grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable instrument like a forceps or a saw, then use what is at your disposal; remove the pieces that are stuck in the bone from their roughness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do your best to put it back in its place, then moisten the bandage with astringent black wine, and wrap it properly; do not put any wax or other substance on the wound that could cause decay; then administer stars (possibly herbs or medications) after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and clean the area around it according to the size of the wound, and take good care so that the wound is not constricted by the bandage; and often, through ignorance, people have caused patients great harm, or even death, or severe decay, and these binding should be softer and more gentle than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is severe or deep, and you doubt that a bad accident may occur, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, if it is not suitable to put on bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloth, and bind it tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is bowing or sinking, then remove what you have put on top of it and apply a healing dressing to the wound, such as a four-part ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bow of the bone moves slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for a long time and cannot heal but keeps returning to the bowed state, knowing that there may be small pieces of bone, you must then clean the wound thoroughly, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in its place, or any other kind of corruption, you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open in the member, such as the bone of the calf or the shoulder, or other similar bones of great members, do not pull it, for often death comes from it, but leave it until it putrefies; perhaps after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; if not, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a painful sight to see the shape of the member; and perhaps it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must treat it: if we administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, ace, and similar ones, make sure to press any of these things, or all of them together, and preserve them with astringent wine or with an abundance of heat or with cold; place them on the affected area firmly, and do not loosen them for several days; then dislocate it and begin again with another, until the swelling is gone; or tie it tightly to a well-made pad; for the property of a pad is that it draws out all swelling from the limbs; and if the dislocation has already become hardened like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess above, and treating the remaining part until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate member remains, it occurs for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not bound as it should be; or because there are too many bands and it cannot assume the normal movement of the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or from too great movements, not in their proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the blood multiplies within him; then administer baths, and give pleasure and comfort; then apply lead to the member, so that the lead attracts great movement, and often wash it with cold water, until the movement reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Both members twisted after the dislocation.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the members are twisted after reduction, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish ones who say one must break the member all over again; many fools have done this in our land. Such practices are blameworthy and cause great harm, perhaps even death. However, if the contusions and torture are fresh, then they should be treated with hot water or soft herbs such as chamomile leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and apply a mollifying poultice, well-prepared like a good plaster, and take the mucilage of chamomile and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice from it. Or you can use fig extracts, crushed with colon powder, and other medicines that lessen inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the node broken by rubbing it continually and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the distortion is inflamed and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be broken with iron, then it must be covered with a light, precise incision up to the bone; apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations are caused by a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at any time, it is necessary to bring the limb back into its proper position as soon as possible.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if the dislocation is delayed, the limb swells, and by chance it is reset at pain, it is not advisable to move it at that hour when it is swollen; in this way, many times pain and other ailments are caused; however, as soon as it happens, make the patient better, then leave it until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, and reset it gently, caring for each member as best suits its condition.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the upper body from the foot up.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It first happens that the jaws become dislocated and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly out of place, somewhat bent, or completely dislocated, hanging down towards the chin, and spilling saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be closed, nor can the person speak, as their tongue is also affected.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns on its own due to the body's natural movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it hastily, and do not delay; in such a way that the minister places the head with the sick person, and pulls the mirrors towards one of his hands to the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, so the dislocation is from two parts; and let the other two hands be drawn away, to make it even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mirrors be made even, until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns to its place, especially when both mandibles are together, then apply hot water and oil, gently resetting it; do not delay in returning it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well, without pain, he should place moistened bandages on it, made from rose oil and wax; then gently bind them with soft cords; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his feet between two cushions, so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor exert himself more, but eat light food until the pain is gone and the jaw is healed; and then he can drink and eat as desired.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper position within an hour and are not aligned correctly, then fever and sore habits may occur, along with intestinal complications, and perhaps vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is a disaster; and many die from it, in the ninth day.
de la forcelle	De la forcelle" translates directly to "of the
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forcelle cannot be realigned from any side within the continuity of itself and the worse, it is never relieved towards the outside, and feels very painful.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint with the palm of his hand, and it returns; then he applies the plaster and the bandage, and tightens it; and the limb that is towards the neck cannot be realigned; if not, and if it does not realign even once, then you must reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and the bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus same is done with the shoulder joint when it is out of place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the acromion end; and the second is at the part of the scapula; and sometimes it dislocates at the top, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside near the nerves; and it most often dislocates towards the acromion, especially in those with little muscle mass, for them it happens sharply; to those with sufficient muscle, it occurs barely, and retreats barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that there is a blow or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and thinks it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary for you to test it, until you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And the dislocation is known when it deviates towards the joint, and it makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their diversity manifest; and you will find in the top of the shoulder a hollow, and by touching the base of the shoulder, as if it were one, the patient cannot bring his hand to his side or move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, and not hidden, as you can see clearly by touching; and this type of dislocation is not only for immediate correction, when it is new, or if the entrapped part is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's shoulder, then positions his thumbs underneath the joint, and pulls the joint upward with force; and he lifts his hand and extends it upwards, then puts his thumbs underneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If, however, it does not come as described above, after a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and apply gently softening and soothing remedies such as an infusion of althae, fenugreek, and melilote in water, and let him rest. Then, have the patient lie on his back and place a piece of equal thickness of wool underneath the affected shoulder, not too soft nor too hard, then position the heel of the healthy foot on top of it, and gently pull the head of the injured shoulder upward, while also pulling the hand of the patient with a firm but gentle motion; another assistant should hold the head of the shoulder to prevent any movement. The shoulder will return to its proper place, as you will see if you follow this method: and make sure that you have a stronger man present who is larger than the patient; he should be positioned directly opposite the affected side, pull the shoulder blade away from the joint of the injured shoulder, and pull it upward, while another assistant pulls the hand of the patient downward towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy thing is laid upon him, the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also adjusted in another way: take a long stick and place it in the ground so that its tip is as sharp as a pistol, but not too thick or too thin; then place it from under the patient, but with soft cloth above, and the patient's arm fully extended towards the opposite side, and the joint will return to its place; and if it does not want to come back for all the reasons we have mentioned, make this treatment: take a stick of two arms' length and four fingers' width that has a pointed end to completely enter the joint from below, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the patient flat on his back, so that the affected area is not pressed, then place a firm support under the affected limb; extend one arm above the afflicted area, and bind the aid to the affected part, placing the arm across the wrist of the hand, then put the arm over a wide scale, and let the hands hang down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is aligned in any way, it is necessary that you place under the joint a thread of equal wool, then apply the plaster made of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then stretch the joint gently, and tie the bandage again on the plaster, and embrace the hand to the collarbone, and let the hands remain in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; then after a few days or seven, he moves it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stuck due to moisture or any other reason, it is necessary that you administer fire cautery in three places, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the joint comes loose and he cannot raise his arm high, then know that the nerve in the shoulder is damaged or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst part, and the joints, or behind, is often caused by a sudden jerk, stretching of the hands, and it should be treated immediately as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing, the joint becomes stiff in the limb and its movement is delayed; if the patient uses it repeatedly, as long as the stiffness persists, it will eventually return to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation thus:
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocated joint is weakened at the ends, and the ends return; if it is weakened from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected, for it can be clearly seen and felt; it should be treated according to its form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach to its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the abscess closes and does not reappear, for if it reappears, it will be difficult to reset it, especially when it is at the back; then it is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and perhaps even leading to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be brought back as it was before, that you stretch his hand with both of yours; and his arms are extended, and the palms facing each other according to the cost around, from top to bottom, and bring the joint together at his fingers, either at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to its original position, and bring the base of the palm towards the affected joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and have the second minister extend the arm, and stretch it tightly so that it does not move during the extension. Then turn the arm in each direction after wrapping a double long and wide cloth around it. When you observe the joint where it is connected to his hand, rub it with some oil to soften the joint, then bring the joint together until it returns to its place. Once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, tighten the bandage, and keep it on the patient's neck for several days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, it loosens the ligament and leaves it; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, repeat the binding and the ligament, and leave it thus for several days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels pain after resetting the joint, and it becomes stiff, bathe and massage it gently, pressing until it is relieved; or apply a grease-soaked woolen compress to the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and immerse the limb in a bath; and when it is warm, rub the joint temperately, reapply the compress, and then take another bath; do this two or three times until healed; and if you see that it still feels cold, wrap fine moistened hot wool around it and press; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint, once reduced, is less stable than others. Nevertheless, it must be held in place gently, immediately after reduction, so that the swelling does not increase or an abscess does not form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is such that you place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the patient's fingers, and ensure they are straightened, so that the palm rests on the joint, holding it until it returns to its proper position. However, you must check if it is in its original place; then, place the patient with the back of their hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient lay his back on his hand on a table, and look closely at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good. Otherwise, if the strain of soothing plasters on abscesses ceases, and it does not start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if the patient cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place for any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and neither the pain nor any part can be healed: then know that a nerve or an artery is cut; and there is no other mechanism to draw out the case except by delicate cautery, and perhaps there is nothing else worth trying.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, if you put on the plaster as we have said, then pull it and leave it for a day, then loosen it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it properly and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moisture to it and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The fingers of the hand should never be dislocated at each joint, neither at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then, they are dislocated and brought together gently until they return to their original position, then hold the top of the finger, and pull it towards the part where it is disjoined; leave it for a day, and then repeat this process each day; and do not tie it, as we have said, but loosen it each day and move it, and reconnect it; and do so repeatedly until it is tight, and also do the same if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and follow the same steps until it heals; and do the same for any other part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient often dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the patient's limbs jump uncontrollably, unable to hold them still; often, one or both arms or legs become weak, and sometimes the spine is bent in four parts; the bend at the back is called "gypsiness". The cure for this is to reward the gypsiness if it has been present from childhood; there is no cure or treatment for this condition.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the ancient ways of healing speak of in great words, but they offer no real benefit; however, I have abridged it according to my understanding and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the foot first, no one has any health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and it is only the cure properly coming from behind that can heal it, as I say; and it is that the patient should be stretched on his face equally in the first position, and have a pull underneath him so he does not twist; then I insert a stick in the middle of the head in the earth-formed shape, and another at the knee, and tie a loose band around the affected parts of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the thighs, and at the ankles; and these ministers know the bands, one on the head and the others on the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well secured, the stick as we have said, and the observer places his palms on the formed spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut the wall from behind, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the middle of the table over the spine, and put both feet on the other end of the table, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it moving, do this with a stick that turns in your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two long splints, one for the patient's head and one for each foot, and between each splint make an incision from above and below, leaving a space of about a palm length; and in each splint make a hole through which the stick turns, and ensure the splints are firmly fastened so they do not move; and between the two splints there should be one turning stick, with two small splints a palm length long, to turn the stick; then tie the stick that is among the splints to the head end, and the other end to the feet at the other turning stick, and each helper turns their stick along the whole length, and the master ensures the spine is straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which should adhere to the skin of the joint and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle relief until they are healed; and if any thing happens at the end of their healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, using the method that we have mentioned before; and never apply a piece of plaster, nor let there be any appearance on the rear spine, thinking it dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have presumptuousness: perhaps death might come as a result.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the thigh and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike the other joints; and the joint of the thigh is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, it's less misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is such that when you join the injured leg with the healthy one, if it's longer, and opens the knee of the patient more than the healthy one, and they cannot bend their knee; this is due to the inflammation around the abscess above, because the bone in the thigh comes closer.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who is destined to die, it is that this accident goes against what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences it beforehand, if he has a strong leg according to its fulfillment; nevertheless, do not bend the knee too much without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot do so before, and he retains his urine, and the ankle swells, and when he tries to walk, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences it afterwards, if he cannot spread or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the movement of the thigh is towards the inside, opposite the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They should reset this appearance of dislocation if it is that the dislocation is old and persists according to its nature, as there is no cure; and one must not let him be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you must act quickly, returning the joint to its proper position both internally and externally, and then aligning it to the right and left; perhaps it will return on its own, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must then use a strong strap, extending the leg strongly at the knee or binding it to the loins; another minister should place his hand from above in such a way that he bends the patient's hands downwards towards their heels, then pull tightly with a soft strap on the calf; others should hold the head with a strap; and all stretch upwards and downwards simultaneously, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, remaining in that position.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all three conditions, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If the dislocation is in the hip joint, it is necessary to treat this condition. The patient should be placed on their healthy side, then tie a ligature on the root of the thigh, and the joint that is above the wound; then stretch the ligament towards the wound and towards the strength; then ask another helper to support the patient's arms, embrace the large joint of the affected thigh, and extend it in a different direction. It will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner we have said, then you should bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and both knees; then let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the others; then hang it over a pole, and let it be suspended two arms' length above the ground; then command the assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and have other assistants hanging with the patient, who embrace the thigh, for the joint now moves harmoniously.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is external, if the patient lies down as we have said in the case of the luxation, then tighten the ligature properly on the sick leg and also on the foot; then place two hot coals, one at the head and another at the foot; then insert a hot coal between the thighs of the patient in the form of the dislocation. And wrap moist cloths around him so he does not feel the pain, then have each assistant stretch towards him and check to ensure that the dislocation is equal in both hands.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg forcefully, as I have said; and alleviate the patient's pain from being on the affected side, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the affected leg downwards, nor to raise it up onto the ground, but rather it must remain as it was when the hip was dislocated, as we have said before, gently on both sides; and place it on its face, with the joint extended as we have said earlier, and press upon it at the table. And this will be achieved once the patient extends their legs and they are even; then tighten the stockings, apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the plaster again; and gently encourage the patient to move, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and posteriorly; but not anteriorly.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not return to its place at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and place his foot on yours. Then take the knee in your palms and draw between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee joint; and another minister extends the foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it gently returns the leg to its knee; and apply a poultice, and raise the leg at the knee, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then release it; and let not the patient move about, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all extended, apply a strong stretch, as we have said in the treatment of the spine, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither entirely dislocated nor fully located, and it is both internally and externally displaced.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tenderness in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is gentle, and one should gently extend their hand towards the affected side when it is slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from all sides, you should make the patient lie straight and hold the leg outside their foot with the minister; then take the foot in your right hand and pull twice, then stretch it upwards nicely, and push the foot back up; do this twice as we have said, by stretching and pulling the foot; if it comes back, that's good; if not, continue the work, for it will come back; and if it cannot return like that, make the patient lie on their stomach on the ground, and insert a firm stick between their thighs, and wrap the drapes around them so they do not hurt the patient; then have the ministers hold the thigh, and others stretch the foot to its fingers or joint where it is held by the foot; then each minister stretches equally, and the stick should be between the patient's thighs to keep them still when stretched; then put both hands on the dislocation for the patient, and another minister holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return more easily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the fracture is healed to a certain point, apply an ointment and bandage, stretch the limb, secure the foot to the leg, and hold fast the ligaments behind the ankle so they are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments loosen, release them; then dislodge it on the third day or a quarter of that time, and the patient should walk within four days; and if he continues beyond this point, it is not lucky for him to recover further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses occur, it is necessary to soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are healthy.
des dois	Of the two (parts)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the eyes are dislocated, if they need to be nicely extended without effort, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the dislocation is in any other part of the body, it is necessary that you place the patient on a flat or straight table and put your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press with your foot form until it returns; and when it is even and nothing opens, place a two-legged table under the sole of the foot, then pull with the form and leave it for three days, then release it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies if you are not careful in treatment: so be neither presumptuous nor hasty, unless you are skilled in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and be neither cruel nor quick to judge; begin with gentle remedies for the abscess, and leave the patient in God's care, if you see no hope of recovery. And when there is hope, immediately realign the limb as best you can, so that the abscess does not grow worse. And once the limb is back in place, apply gentle remedies to the abscess, and treat the wound accordingly; if there are broken bones or small bones displaced, treat it as we have said for simple ailments; and beware of falling into despair, as I have advised, for this will be to your benefit according to your Creator's will, and for the knowledge of your arms and body.
